<div class="front"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="actHd" id="aT-">Adoption of Children Act</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="chapNo">(CHAPTER 4)</td></tr></tbody></table><p class="origSrc">(Original Enactment: Ordinance 18 of 1939)</p><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdHdr">REVISED EDITION 2012</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdTxt">(31st March 2012)</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="longTitle" id="al-">An Act to make provision for the adoption of infants.</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="cDate">[29th December 1939]</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="body"><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr1-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Short title</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>1.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;This Act may be cited as the Adoption of Children Act.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr2-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Interpretation</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>2.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Act, unless the context otherwise requires&nbsp;—<table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“court” means the High Court or a Family Court;<div class="amendNote">[Act 27 of 2014 wef 01/10/2014]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“father”, in relation to an illegitimate infant, means the natural father;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“parent”, in relation to an illegitimate infant, does not include the natural father;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Registrar”, in relation to any court, means the Registrar of that court.<div class="amendNote">[9/72]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr3-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Power to make adoption orders</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>3.</strong><a name="pr3-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Upon an application in the prescribed manner by any person desirous of being authorised to adopt an infant who has never been married, the court may, subject to the provisions of this Act, make an order (referred to in this Act as an adoption order) authorising the applicant to adopt that infant.</span><a name="pr3-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;A person so authorised to adopt the infant and an infant authorised to be adopted are referred to in this Act as an adopter and an adopted child respectively, and infant means a person under the age of 21 years.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr3-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where an application for an adoption order is made by 2 spouses jointly, the court may make the order authorising the 2 spouses jointly to adopt an infant.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr3-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;An adoption order may be made authorising the adoption of an infant by the mother or father of the infant, either alone or jointly with her or his spouse.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr3-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;Except as provided in this section, no adoption order shall be made authorising more than one person to adopt an infant.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr4-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Restrictions on making adoption orders</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>4.</strong><a name="pr4-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;An adoption order shall not be made in any case where&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the applicant is under the age of 25 years; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the applicant is less than 21 years older than the infant in respect of whom the application is made.</td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr4-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Notwithstanding subsection&nbsp;(1), it shall be lawful for the court, if it thinks fit, to make an adoption order&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">where the applicant is under the age of 25 years and less than 21 years older than the infant if&nbsp;—<table class="p2_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr id="pr4-ps2-p1a-p2i-"><td class="p2No">(i)</td><td class="p2Txt">the applicant and the infant are within the prohibited degrees of consanguinity; or</td></tr><tr id="pr4-ps2-p1a-p2ii-"><td class="p2No">(ii)</td><td class="p2Txt">in other special circumstances which justify as an exceptional measure the making of an adoption order where the applicant and the infant are not within the prohibited degrees of consanguinity;</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">in the case of an application by 2 spouses jointly where one of the spouses and the infant are within the prohibited degrees of consanguinity, notwithstanding that the other spouse is under the age of 25 years and less than 21 years older than the infant; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">in the case of an application by 2 spouses jointly where neither spouse is within the prohibited degrees of consanguinity with the infant, notwithstanding that one or both the spouses are less than 21 years older than the infant.<div class="amendNote">[9/72]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;An adoption order shall not be made in any case where the sole applicant is a male and the infant in respect of whom the application is made is a female unless the court is satisfied that there are special circumstances which justify as an exceptional measure the making of an adoption order.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;An adoption order shall not be made except with the consent of every person or body who is a parent or guardian of the infant in respect of whom the application is made or who has the actual custody of the infant or who is liable to contribute to the support of the infant; but the court may dispense with any consent required by this subsection if the court is satisfied that the person whose consent is to be dispensed with&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">has abandoned, neglected, persistently ill-treated the infant or cannot be found and that reasonable notice of the application for an adoption order has been given to the parent or guardian where the parent or guardian can be found;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">is unfit by reason of any physical or mental incapacity to have the care and control of the infant, that the unfitness is likely to continue indefinitely and that reasonable notice of the application for an adoption order has been given to the parent or guardian; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">ought, in the opinion of the court and in all the circumstances of the case to be dispensed with, notwithstanding that such person may have made suitable initial arrangements for the infant by placing the infant under the care of the authorities of a home for children and young persons, the protector under the Children and Young Persons Act (Cap. 38) or some other person.<div class="amendNote">[9/72]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;An adoption order shall not be made upon the application of one of 2 spouses without the consent of the other of them; except that court may dispense with any consent required by this subsection if satisfied that the person whose consent is to be dispensed with cannot be found or is incapable of giving such consent or that the spouses have separated and are living apart and that the separation is likely to be permanent.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps6-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(6)&nbsp;&nbsp;An adoption order shall not be made in favour of any applicant who is not resident in Singapore or in respect of any infant who is not so resident.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps7-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(7)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purpose of subsection&nbsp;(6), an infant shall be deemed not to be resident in Singapore&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">if he is authorised or permitted to remain in Singapore by virtue of a visit pass, a student’s pass or a special pass issued by the Controller of Immigration, irrespective of the number of occasions such a pass is issued to him or renewed; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">if his presence in Singapore is unlawful under the provisions of the Immigration Act (Cap. 133) or the regulations made thereunder.<div class="amendNote">[3/85]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr5-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Matters with respect to which court to be satisfied</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>5.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;The court before making an adoption order shall be satisfied&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">that every person whose consent is necessary under this Act and whose consent is not dispensed with has consented to and understands the nature and effect of the adoption order for which application is made, and in particular in the case of any parent understands that the effect of the adoption order will be permanently to deprive him or her of his or her parental rights;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">that the order if made will be for the welfare of the infant, due consideration being for this purpose given to the wishes of the infant, having regard to the age and understanding of the infant; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">that the applicant has not received or agreed to receive, and that no person has made or given, or agreed to make or give to the applicant, any payment or other reward in consideration of the adoption except such as the court may sanction.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr6-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Terms and conditions of order</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>6.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;The court in an adoption order may impose such terms and conditions as the court may think fit and in particular may require the adopter by bond or otherwise to make for the adopted child such provision, if any, as in the opinion of the court is just and expedient.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr7-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Effect of adoption order</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>7.</strong><a name="pr7-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Upon an adoption order being made —<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">all rights, duties, obligations and liabilities of the parent or parents, guardian or guardians of the adopted child, in relation to the future custody, maintenance and education of the adopted child, including all rights to appoint a guardian or to consent or give notice of dissent to marriage shall be extinguished;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">all such rights, duties, obligations and liabilities shall vest in and be exercisable by and enforceable against the adopter as though the adopted child was a child born to the adopter in lawful wedlock; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">in respect of the same matters and in respect of the liability of a child to maintain its parents, the adopted child shall stand to the adopter exclusively in the position of a child born to the adopter in lawful wedlock,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">except that in any case where 2 spouses are the adopters, such spouses shall, in respect of the matters in paragraphs&nbsp;(<em>a</em>) to (<em>c</em>) and for the purpose of the jurisdiction of any court to make orders as to the custody and maintenance of and right of access to children, stand to each other and to the adopted child in the same relation as they would have stood if they had been the lawful father and mother of the adopted child, and the adopted child shall stand to them respectively in the same relation as a child would have stood to a lawful father and mother respectively.</td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr7-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where, at any time after the making of an adoption order —<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the adopter or the adopted person or any other person dies intestate in respect of any movable or immovable property, that property shall devolve in all respects as if the adopted person were the child of the adopter born in lawful wedlock and not the child of any other person;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">in any disposition of movable or immovable property made, whether by instrument inter vivos or by will (including codicil) after the date of an adoption order&nbsp;—<table class="p2_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr id="pr7-ps2-p1b-p2i-"><td class="p2No">(i)</td><td class="p2Txt">any reference (whether express or implied) to the child or children of the adopter shall, unless the contrary intention appears, be construed as, or as including, a reference to the adopted person;</td></tr><tr id="pr7-ps2-p1b-p2ii-"><td class="p2No">(ii)</td><td class="p2Txt">any reference (whether express or implied) to the child or children of the adopted person’s natural parents or either of them shall, unless the contrary intention appears, be construed as not being, or as not including, a reference to the adopted person; and</td></tr><tr id="pr7-ps2-p1b-p2iii-"><td class="p2No">(iii)</td><td class="p2Txt">any reference (whether express or implied) to a person related to the adopted person in any degree shall, unless the contrary intention appears, be construed as a reference to the person who would be related to him in that degree if he were the child of the adopter born in lawful wedlock and were not the child of any other person.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr7-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where an adopted child or the spouse or issue of an adopted child takes any interest in movable or immovable property under a disposition by the adopter or under any intestacy, or where an adopter takes any interest in movable or immovable property under a disposition by an adopted child or the spouse or issue of an adopted child, or under the intestacy of an adopted child or the spouse or issue of an adopted child, any estate or other duty which becomes leviable in respect thereof shall be payable at the same rate as if the adopted child had been a child born to the adopter in lawful wedlock.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr7-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of this section, “disposition” means an assurance of any interest in property by any instrument whether inter vivos or by will including codicil.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr7-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of section&nbsp;20 or 21 of the Civil Law Act (Cap.&nbsp;43), a person shall be deemed to be the parent or child of the person deceased notwithstanding that he was only related to him in consequence of adoption; and accordingly in deducing any relationship which under the provisions of that section is included within the meaning of the expressions “parent” and “child” an adopted child shall be treated as being, or as having been, the legitimate offspring of his adopter.<div class="amendNote">[11/87]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr7-ps6-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(6)&nbsp;&nbsp;Notwithstanding anything in this section, trustees or personal representatives —<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">may convey or distribute any movable or immovable property to or among the persons entitled thereto without having ascertained that no adoption order has been made by virtue of which any person is or may be entitled to any interest therein; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">shall not be liable to any such person of whose claim they have not had notice at the time of the conveyance or distribution,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">but nothing in this subsection shall prejudice the right of any such person to follow the property, or any property representing it, into the hands of any person, other than a purchaser, who may have received it.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr7-ps7-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(7)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where an adoption order is made in respect of a person who has been previously adopted, the previous adoption shall be disregarded for the purposes of this section in relation to the devolution of any property on the death of a person dying intestate after the date of the subsequent adoption order and in relation to any disposition of property made after that date.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr7-ps8-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(8)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purpose of the law relating to marriage, an adopter and the person whom he has been authorised to adopt under an adoption order and all children and adopted children of the adopter shall be deemed to be within the prohibited degrees of consanguinity; and this subsection shall continue to have effect notwithstanding that some person other than the adopter is authorised by a subsequent order to adopt the same infant.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr7-ps9-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(9)&nbsp;&nbsp;An adoption order shall not by itself affect the citizenship of the adopted child.<div class="amendNote">[9/72]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr8-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Power to make interim orders</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>8.</strong><a name="pr8-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Upon any application for an adoption order, the court may postpone the determination of the application and may make an interim order (which shall not be an adoption order for the purposes of this Act) giving the custody of the infant to the applicant for a period not exceeding 2 years by way of a probationary period upon such terms as regards provision for the maintenance and education and supervision of the welfare of the infant and otherwise as the court may think fit.</span><a name="pr8-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;All such consents as are required to an adoption order shall be necessary to an interim order but subject to a like power on the part of the court to dispense with any such consent.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr9-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Power to make subsequent order in respect of infant already subject to an order</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>9.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;An adoption order or an interim order may be made in respect of an infant who has already been the subject of an adoption order, and, upon any application for such further adoption order, the adopter or adopters under the adoption order last previously made shall, if living, be deemed to be the parent or parents of the infant for all the purposes of this Act.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr10-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Procedure</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>10.</strong><a name="pr10-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Family Justice Rules Committee constituted under section 46(1) of the Family Justice Act 2014 may make Family Justice Rules&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to prescribe any matter which may be prescribed under this Act;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to provide for the manner in which any application to the court is to be made, heard and determined; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to provide for all matters of procedure and incidental matters under this Act.<div class="amendNote">[Act 27 of 2014 wef 01/01/2015]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr10-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Family Justice Rules may, instead of providing for any matter, refer to any provision made or to be made about that matter by practice directions issued for the time being by the registrar of the Family Justice Courts.<div class="amendNote">[Act 27 of 2014 wef 01/01/2015]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr10-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purpose of any application under this Act and subject to the Family Justice Rules, the court shall appoint some person or body to act as a guardian in adoption of the infant upon the hearing of the application with the duty of safeguarding the interests of the infant before the court.<div class="amendNote">[42/2005]</div><div class="amendNote">[Act 27 of 2014 wef 01/01/2015]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr11-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Restriction on payments</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>11.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;It shall not be lawful for any adopter or for any parent or guardian except with the sanction of the court to receive any payment or other reward in consideration of the adoption of any infant under this Act or for any person to make or give or agree to make or give to any adopter or to any parent or guardian any such payment or reward.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr12-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Registration of adopted children</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>12.</strong><a name="pr12-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where an adoption order has been made, the Registrar of the court by which the adoption order was made shall forthwith send to the Registrar-General of Births and Deaths a notice in the form set out in the&nbsp;Schedule, setting out the following particulars so far as they are known to the court:<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the full name of the child before the making of the adoption order;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the full name of the child conferred by the adoption order;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the date and place of birth of the child;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>d</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the birth certificate registration number or entry number of the last preceding adoption or re-registration number;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>e</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the sex of the child;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>f</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the names of the natural or last preceding adopting parents of the child;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>g</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the name or names and the occupation and address of the adopting parent or adopting parents;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>h</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the date and country of birth, race and dialect group, nationality and citizenship, and Singapore identity card number of the adopting parent or adopting parents;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>i</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the maiden name of the adopting mother if she is or has been married;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>j</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">in the case of adoption by a single adopter, whether the adoptive parent wishes that the words “adoptive father” or “adoptive mother” as the case may require, appear on the face of any certified copy of the entry of birth of the child issued after the birth has been registered under this section;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>k</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the date of the adoption order and a description of the court by which it was made;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>l</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">such other particulars as may be required by the Registrar-General.<div class="amendNote">[9/72]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr12-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where —<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the precise date of the infant’s birth is not proved to the satisfaction of the court, the court shall determine the probable date of his birth and the date so determined shall be specified in the order as the date of his birth; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the country of birth of the infant is not proved to the satisfaction of the court, the particulars of that country may be omitted from the order and from the entry in the register maintained by the Registrar-General.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr12-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Upon receipt of the form referred to in subsection&nbsp;(1), the Registrar-General shall if the birth of the adopted child has been registered in Singapore cause the entry in the relevant register of births to be marked with the word “Adopted”. Particulars as to the birth of the child shall then be registered separately substituting the name conferred by the adoption for the name of the child prior to adoption, and recording the name, address and description of each adopting parent in substitution for the particulars as to the natural or last adopting parents.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr12-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;In any case where the birth of the adopted child has not been registered in Singapore, the Registrar-General, upon being satisfied as to the correctness of the information supplied to him as to the date and place of birth of the child, shall register particulars as to the birth of the child in accordance with the procedure in subsection&nbsp;(3).</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr12-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where a copy of the entry as to the birth of any child to which this section relates is required for any purpose, the Registrar-General, subject to any regulations as to payment of fees as are prescribed, shall supply a copy of the last entry made pursuant to subsection&nbsp;(3) omitting in the copy the word “Adopted” that appears in the original or former entry.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr12-ps6-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(6)&nbsp;&nbsp;No person shall be permitted to inspect any such original or former entry, or to take a copy of such original or former entry unless that person has certified, and the Registrar-General is satisfied, that the particulars recorded in the original or former entry are material for the purpose for which the inspection is required.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr12-ps7-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(7)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where on 15th May 1972 an adoption order has already been made in respect of an infant, the Registrar-General shall upon application being made by either of the adopting parents, or in the event of both adopting parents being dead, by the adopted child register particulars as to the birth of the child in accordance with subsection&nbsp;(3) and upon registration, subsection&nbsp;(5) shall apply to any copy of an entry as to the birth of the adopted child.<div class="amendNote">[9/72]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr12-ps8-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(8)&nbsp;&nbsp;The copy of the entry as to the birth of the child supplied by the Registrar-General under subsection&nbsp;(5) shall have the same effect in law as a copy of any entry as to the birth of a child who is not adopted.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr12-ps9-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(9)&nbsp;&nbsp;Rules made by the Minister under the Registration of Births and Deaths Act (Cap. 267) may make provision as to the duties to be performed by Registrars, Supervising Deputy Registrars and Deputy Registrars in the administration of this Act.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr12-ps10-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(10)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Adopted Children Register maintained under section&nbsp;11 repealed by the Adoption of Children (Amendment) Act 1972 (Act&nbsp;9 of 1972) shall cease to be maintained and no extracts therefrom shall be issued except by an order of court.<div class="amendNote">[9/72]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr12-ps11-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(11)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Registrar-General shall keep such other registers and books, and make such entries therein as may be necessary to record and make traceable the connection between any entry in the Adopted Children Register previously maintained under section&nbsp;11 repealed by the Adoption of Children (Amendment) Act 1972 and any entry in the registers of births made pursuant to this section, but the registers and books kept under this subsection shall not be, nor shall any index thereof be, open to public inspection or search nor except under an order of court shall the Registrar furnish any person with any information contained in or with any copy or extract from any such registers or books.<div class="amendNote">[9/72]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div class="tail"><div class="schedule" style="max-width: 620px;"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="sHdr" id="Sc-">THE SCHEDULE</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="SbodyRefs" id="Sc-rf-">Section&nbsp;12(1)</td></tr></tbody></table><table <div class="front"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="actHd" id="aT-">Betting Act</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="chapNo">(CHAPTER 21)</td></tr></tbody></table><p class="origSrc">(Original Enactment: Ordinance 30 of 1960)</p><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdHdr">REVISED EDITION 2011</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdTxt">(31st December 2011)</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="longTitle" id="al-">An Act to suppress common betting-houses, betting in public places and bookmaking.</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="cDate">[20th May 1960]</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="body"><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr1-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Short title</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>1.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;This Act may be cited as the Betting Act.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr2-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Interpretation</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>2.</strong><a name="pr2-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Act, unless the context&nbsp;otherwise requires —<table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“access” includes access through the telephone, by post or by telegram;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“betting information centre” means any place kept or used for receiving or transmitting by telephone or other means any information relating to any horse-race or other sporting event for the purpose of betting or wagering in contravention of this Act;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“bookmaker” means any person who, whether on his own account or as penciller, runner, employee or agent for any other person, receives or negotiates bets or wagers whether on a cash or on a credit basis and whether for money or money’s worth, or who in any manner holds himself out or permits himself to be held out in any manner as a person who receives or negotiates those bets or wagers; but does not include a club, its officers or employees or any other person or organisation operating or conducting a totalisator or pari-mutuel or any other system or method of cash or credit betting authorised under section&nbsp;22;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“common betting-house” means&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">any place kept or used for betting or wagering on any event or contingency of or relating to any horse-race or other sporting event to which the public or any class of the public has or may have access;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">any place kept or used for habitual betting or wagering on any such event or contingency as aforesaid, whether the public has, or may have, access thereto or not; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">any place used by a bookmaker for the purpose of receiving or negotiating bets or wagers on any such event or contingency as aforesaid whether the bets or wagers reach the bookmaker by the hand of the person placing the bet or his agent or the bookmaker’s agent or through the telephone or by post or by telegram or by any other means;</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“equipment” has the same meaning as in the Telecommunications Act (Cap.&nbsp;323);</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“penciller” means a person who helps a bookmaker to keep his accounts or record of bets in connection with horse-races;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“place” means any house, office, room or building, and any place or spot, whether open or enclosed, and includes a ship, boat, or other vessel whether afloat or not, and any vehicle;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“runner” means a person employed by a bookmaker to collect and settle bets either on salary or on commission basis;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“sporting event” includes any race, fight, game, sport or exercise;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“telecommunication system” has the same meaning as in the Telecommunications Act. <div class="amendNote">[8/86; 43/99; 13/2004]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr2-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;A place shall be deemed to be used for a purpose if it is used for that purpose on only one occasion.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;A place shall be deemed to be used for habitual betting or wagering if betting or wagering is frequently carried on therein, notwithstanding that betting or wagering is not the primary purpose for which that place is normally used.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;Every person who demises or lets for hire a place shall be deemed to be the owner thereof.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;A common betting-house shall be deemed to be a common nuisance and contrary to law.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr2A-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Act not applicable to remote gambling</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>2A.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;The provisions of this Act do not apply to or in relation to any remote gambling within the meaning of the Remote Gambling Act 2014.<div class="amendNote">[Act 34 of 2014 wef 02/02/2015]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr3-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Offences relating to common betting-houses and betting information centres</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>3.</strong><a name="pr3-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any person who&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">being the owner or occupier, or having the use temporarily or otherwise thereof, keeps or uses a place as a common betting-house or betting information centre;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">permits a place of which he is the owner or occupier or of which he has the use temporarily or otherwise, to be kept or used as a common betting-house or betting information centre;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">has the care or management of or in any manner assists in the management or in the business of, a place kept or used as a common betting-house or betting information centre;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>d</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">receives directly or indirectly any money or valuable thing, for or in respect of any bet or wager on any such event or contingency, as is mentioned in this Act, in a common betting-house or betting information centre; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>e</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">announces, exhibits or publishes, or causes to be announced, exhibited or published, either orally or by means of any letter, circular, telegram, placard, handbill, card, print, writing, design, sign, advertisement or otherwise that a place is opened, kept or used as a common betting-house or betting information centre in Singapore or elsewhere, or in any other manner invites or solicits any person to commit a breach of any of the provisions of this Act,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">shall be guilty of an offence and shall be liable on conviction to a fine of not less than $20,000 and not more than $200,000 and shall also be punished with imprisonment for a term not exceeding 5 years. </td></tr></tbody></table><div class="amendNote">[8/86]</div></span><a name="pr3-ps1A-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(1A)&nbsp;&nbsp;Subsection&nbsp;(1)(<em>e</em>) shall not apply to&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the Singapore Totalisator Board;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any totalisator agency appointed by the Singapore Totalisator Board; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any agent appointed by the Singapore Totalisator Board to operate or conduct any totalisator, lottery, betting or gaming activity.<div class="amendNote">[12/2008]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr3-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any person who occupies or has the use temporarily of a place which is kept or used by another person as a common betting-house or betting information centre shall be presumed until the contrary is proved to have permitted that place to be so kept or used.<div class="amendNote">[8/86]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr4-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Advancing money for conducting business of common betting-house</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>4.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Any person who advances or furnishes money for the purpose of establishing or conducting the business of a common betting-house shall be guilty of an offence and shall be liable on conviction to a fine of not less than $10,000 and not more than $100,000 and shall also be punished with imprisonment for a term not exceeding 5 years. <div class="amendNote">[8/86]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr5-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Betting in a common betting-house</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>5.</strong><a name="pr5-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Except as permitted by an exemption under section&nbsp;22, any person who bets or wagers in a common betting-house, or with a bookmaker in any place or by any means, or who for the purpose of betting or wagering loiters in any place to which the public has or may have access shall be guilty of an offence and shall be liable on conviction to a fine not exceeding $5,000 or to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or to both.<div class="amendNote">[8/86]</div></span><a name="pr5-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;A person found in a common betting-house, or found escaping therefrom on the occasion of its being entered under this Act shall be presumed, until the contrary is proved, to be or to have been betting or wagering therein.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr5-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any person who&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">acts as a bookmaker in any place;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">for the purpose of bookmaking or settling bets loiters in any common betting-house or in any place to which the public has or may have access; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">assists, by giving warning or otherwise, any person committing an offence under this Act to evade arrest or detection,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">shall be guilty of an offence and shall be liable on conviction to a fine of not less than $20,000 and not more than $200,000 and shall also be punished with imprisonment for a term not exceeding 5 years.</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="amendNote">[8/86]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr5-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;When any person is convicted of an offence under this section all books, accounts, documents, telegrams, writings, circulars, cards or other articles used as a subject or means of betting or wagering, or in connection therewith, and all moneys or securities for money found in his possession which a Magistrate’s Court or District Court is of opinion were used or intended to be used for betting or wagering shall be declared by that Court to be forfeited to the State and shall be dealt with accordingly.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr5-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;An offence under subsection&nbsp;(3) shall be a non-bailable arrestable offence and any person making an arrest for such an offence may seize and detain any articles liable to be forfeited.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr5-ps6-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(6)&nbsp;&nbsp;Notwithstanding anything to the contrary in section&nbsp;93 of the Criminal Procedure Code 2010 (Act 15 of 2010) a police officer shall have power to release on bail a person accused of an offence under subsection&nbsp;(3). <div class="amendNote">[21/73; 15/2010]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr6-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Penalty for unlawful announcement of information on horse-race, etc.</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>6.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Any person who for the purpose of betting or wagering in contravention of this Act announces or publishes or causes to be announced or published in any manner information relating to any horse-race or other sporting event shall be guilty of an offence and shall be liable on conviction to a fine of not less than $5,000 and not more than $50,000 and shall also be punished with imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years. <div class="amendNote">[8/86]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr7-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Money paid recoverable</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>7.</strong><a name="pr7-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any money or valuable thing received by any person convicted under section&nbsp;5(3) as a deposit on or in settlement of any bet or wager shall be deemed to have been received to or for the use of the person from whom it was received.</span><a name="pr7-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Such money or valuable thing, or the value thereof, may be recovered accordingly with full costs of suit in any court of competent jurisdiction.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr8-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Presumption against person accepting or receiving stakes, etc.</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>8.</strong><a name="pr8-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any person accepting or receiving bets, stakes or wagers or found in possession of any books, accounts, documents, telegrams, writings, circulars, cards or other articles which are used or appear to have been used or intended to be used in connection with or which relate or appear to relate to the business of a bookmaker shall be presumed until the contrary is proved to be acting as a bookmaker.</span><a name="pr8-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any person who settles or pays money or money’s worth in respect of bets or wagers relating to a horse-race or any other kind of race shall also be presumed until the contrary is proved to be acting as a bookmaker.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr9-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Presumptions</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>9.</strong><a name="pr9-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where in any proceedings under this Act it is proved that any place entered under this Act was provided with 3 or more telephones or telephone lines and&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">was installed with any telecommunication system or equipment which was arranged in such a manner as to suggest that it is or was being used for the receiving or transmitting of any information relating to any horse-race or other sporting event notwithstanding that such telecommunication system or equipment has been disconnected or tampered with;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any person found in a place so entered was erasing, tampering with or destroying any writing, sign, mark or symbol relating to the results or dividends payable on any horse-race or other sporting event; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">2 or more telephone calls were received at any such place enquiring about the results, commentary or dividends payable on any horse-race or other sporting event,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">it shall be presumed, until the contrary is proved, that the place is a betting information centre and that it is so kept, used or permitted to be used by the owner or occupier thereof, and that any other person found in such place is assisting in the business of the betting information centre. </td></tr></tbody></table><div class="amendNote">[8/86]</div></span><a name="pr9-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where in any proceedings under this Act it is proved that&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any document or thing designed, adapted, or intended for use or used for the purpose of betting or wagering was found in any place entered under this Act or upon any person found in such place;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any person found in a place entered under this Act was erasing, tampering with or destroying any writing, sign, mark or symbol relating to bets or wagers on any horse-race or other sporting event; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">2 or more telephone calls were received at any place entered under this Act and the calls relate to the receiving or negotiating of bets or wagers or to any results, commentary or dividends payable on any horse-race or other sporting event,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">it shall be presumed, until the contrary is proved, that the place is a common betting-house and that it is so kept, used or permitted to be used by the owner or occupier thereof, and that any other person found in such place in possession of any such document or thing as is referred to in paragraph&nbsp;(<em>a</em>) is assisting in the management of such common betting-house.</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="amendNote">[8/86]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr10-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Court to make order for demolition of structural contrivances for facilitating betting</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>10.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Whenever it appears to the court upon the trial of any offence under this Act that the place in or in respect of which the offence is alleged to have been committed is a common betting-house and that the place is fitted or provided with any of the means or contrivances mentioned in section&nbsp;9, the court shall order the demolition and destruction of such of them as consist of staircases, doors, partitions, ladders, planks, platforms, posts, palings, bars, bolts and other things which appear to the court to have been specially erected or constructed for the purpose of facilitating the carrying on of betting on the premises.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr11-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Search warrant against premises used as common betting-house</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>11.</strong><a name="pr11-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;A Magistrate or a police officer not below the rank of assistant superintendent on being satisfied, upon written information, and after any further inquiry which he thinks necessary, that there is good reason to believe that any place is kept or used as a common betting-house may by warrant under his hand or by writing under his hand, as the case may be, authorise any person therein named, or any police officer, with such assistance, and by such force, as is necessary, by night or by day, to enter or go to that place and to search the place and all persons found therein, and to seize all books, documents, telegrams, writings, circulars, cards or other articles reasonably supposed to have been used or intended to be used as a subject or means of betting or wagering, or in connection therewith, and all moneys and securities for money which are found in that place or on any such persons, and also to detain all such persons until they and that place have been searched.</span><a name="pr11-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;If any of the things or circumstances which are by this Act made presumptive evidence of guilt are found in such place, or on any person therein, every person therein shall be arrested and taken before a Magistrate’s Court or District Court to be dealt with according to law.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr11-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;All books, documents, telegrams, writings, circulars, cards or other articles used as a subject or means of betting or wagering, or in connection therewith, and all moneys or securities for money, found in a common betting-house, or on any persons found therein, or escaping therefrom, which a Magistrate’s Court or District Court is of opinion were used or intended to be used for betting or wagering, shall be declared by that Court to be forfeited to the State, and shall be dealt with accordingly.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr12-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Search warrant against persons in possession of betting instruments</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>12.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;A Magistrate or a police officer not below the rank of assistant superintendent on being satisfied upon reasonable information and after any inquiry which he may think necessary, that there is good reason to believe that any books, documents, telegrams, writings, circulars, cards or other articles used as a subject or means of betting or wagering, or in connection therewith, are likely to be found on any person may by warrant under his hand or by writing under his hand, as the case may be, order any police officer to arrest and search that person and if any such article is found upon his person he shall be taken before a Magistrate’s Court or District Court to be dealt with according to law.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr13-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Arrest and search upon suspicion</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>13.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Any police officer having reasonable suspicion that such articles as are mentioned in section&nbsp;12 may be found on any person and having reasonable ground for believing that by delay in reporting the offender may escape, may arrest and search that person himself and if any such article is found upon the person searched the offender shall be taken before a police officer not below the rank of sergeant to be dealt with according to law. <div class="amendNote">[21/73]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr14-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Magistrate or police officer may himself enter and search</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>14.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;A Magistrate or a police officer not below the rank of assistant superintendent may himself do what he may under sections&nbsp;11 and 12 authorise a police officer to do whenever the Magistrate or police officer not below the rank of assistant superintendent is competent to issue a warrant or written authority under those sections respectively and also in any of the following cases:<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">if any person has, within the preceding 6 months, been convicted of having kept or used as a common betting-house the place proposed to be entered;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">if the place proposed to be entered is occupied by a club or society which has not been exempted under section&nbsp;22 and he has reason to believe that betting or wagering on horse-races, fights, games or sports is frequently carried on there;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">if he has personal knowledge of such facts and circumstances as satisfy him that there are sufficient grounds for a search under section&nbsp;11; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>d</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">if he receives the required information orally under such circumstances that the object of the search would in his opinion be defeated by the delay necessary for reducing the information to writing to enable a search warrant or written authority to be issued under section&nbsp;11(1).</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr15-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Evidence by police officer to be presumptive evidence</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>15.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;In all proceedings under this Act any evidence given by a police officer that any book, account, document, telegram, writing, circular, card or other article produced before the court had been used or was intended to be used for betting or wagering, shall, until the contrary is proved, be deemed to be sufficient evidence of the fact. <div class="amendNote">[21/73]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr16-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Protection of informers from discovery</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>16.</strong><a name="pr16-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Subject to this section, no information laid under this Act shall be admitted in evidence in any civil or criminal proceedings whatsoever, and no witness shall be obliged or permitted to disclose the name or address of any informer under this Act or state any matter which might lead to his discovery.</span><a name="pr16-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;If any books, documents or papers which are in evidence or liable to inspection in any civil or criminal proceedings whatsoever contain any entry in which any informer is named or described or which might lead to his discovery, the court shall cause all such entries to be concealed from view or to be obliterated so far as is necessary to protect the informer from discovery but no further.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr16-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;If on the trial of any offence under this Act the court, after full inquiry into the case, believes that the informer wilfully made in his information a material statement which he knew or believed to be false or did not believe to be true, the court may require the production of the original information and permit inquiry and require full disclosure concerning the informer.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr17-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Obstruction of police officers</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>17.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Any person who obstructs any police officer in the exercise of any powers under this Act shall be guilty of an offence and shall be liable on conviction to a fine not exceeding $5,000 or to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months or to both. <div class="amendNote">[8/86]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr18-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Examination of offenders</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>18.</strong><a name="pr18-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Whenever 2 or more persons are charged with any offence under this Act, the Magistrate’s Court or District Court may require one or more of them to give evidence as a witness or witnesses for the prosecution.</span><a name="pr18-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any such person who refuses to be sworn or affirmed or to answer any lawful question, shall be dealt with in the same way as witnesses so refusing may by law be dealt with by a Magistrate’s Court or District Court.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr18-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Every person so required to give evidence who, in the opinion of the court, makes true and full discovery of all things as to which he is lawfully examined, shall be entitled to receive a certificate of indemnity under the hand of the Magistrate or Judge, as the case may be, stating that he has made a true and full discovery of all things as to which he was examined, and such certificate shall be a bar to all legal proceedings against him in respect of such things as aforesaid.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr19-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Binding over on second conviction</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>19.</strong><a name="pr19-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;If a person, who has been convicted of an offence under this Act, is again convicted of the same or any other offence under this Act, the Magistrate’s Court or District Court may, in addition to the punishment provided for such offence, make an order requiring him to give security, by bond with one or more sureties, that he will not offend against this Act for such period not exceeding 12 months, as the court thinks fit to fix.</span><a name="pr19-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Every such order shall be made as nearly as may be in the same manner, and shall have the like effect and consequences as if the order were made under section&nbsp;44 of the Criminal Procedure Code 2010 (Act 15 of 2010). <div class="amendNote">[15/2010]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr20-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Jurisdiction of courts</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>20.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;A District Court or a Magistrate’s Court shall have jurisdiction to hear and determine all proceedings under this Act and, notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained in the Criminal Procedure Code 2010 (Act 15 of 2010), shall have power to impose the full penalty or punishment in respect of any offence under this Act. <div class="amendNote">[8/86]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr21-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Stakes</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>21.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Nothing in this Act shall extend to any person receiving or holding any money or valuable thing by way of stakes or deposit to be paid to the winner of any race or lawful sport, game or exercise or to the owner of any horse engaged in a race.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr22-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Exemption</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>22.</strong><a name="pr22-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Minister may, by notification in the <em>Gazette</em>, either generally or in any particular case and subject to such conditions as he may impose, exempt from all or any of the provisions of this Act&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the members and officers of any racing club or association in respect of any totalisator or pari-mutuel betting or any other system or method of cash or credit betting held, promoted, organised, administered or operated by the racing club or association where the betting takes place under the control or supervision of one or more officers of that racing club or association; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any other person or organisation in respect of any system or method of cash or credit betting held, promoted, organised, administered or operated by the person or organisation where the betting takes place under the control or supervision of that person or organisation.<div class="amendNote">[13/2004]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr22-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Every racing club or association exempted under subsection&nbsp;(1) shall place on the totalisator or pari-mutuel under its control or supervision all bets made under any system of cash or credit betting held, promoted, organised, administered or operated by it.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr22-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;It shall be lawful at any time for any racing club or association exempted under subsection&nbsp;(1) to admit members of the public to its premises when racing takes place on payment of an admission fee or to places under the control or supervision of any one or more of its officers either without payment or on payment of an admission fee.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr22-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where an admission fee is charged, the admission fee shall be subject to the payment of duty under the Entertainments Duty Act (Cap. 94). </td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr23-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Reward to informer</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>23.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;The court may direct any fine or any portion of any fine imposed and levied under this Act to be paid to the informer.</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div class="tail"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="LH" id="xv-"><p class="LHHdrNoBold">LEGISLATIVE HISTORY</p><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td on 8 September 2014)</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><td class="event-no-col"></td><td class="event-prompt-col" valign="top"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="colonCol">:</td></tr></tbody></table></td><td valign="top" class="event-content-col"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="contentCol"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="content" <div class="front"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="actHd" id="aT-">Carriage by Air Act</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="chapNo">(CHAPTER 32A)</td></tr></tbody></table><p class="origSrc">(Original Enactment: Act 20 of 1988)</p><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdHdr">REVISED EDITION 2001</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdTxt">(31st December 2001)</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="longTitle" id="al-">An Act to give effect to the provisions of the Warsaw Convention concerning international carriage by air and the Convention as amended by the Hague Protocol and the Montreal Protocol No. 4 and for purposes connected therewith.  <div class="amendNote">[7/99]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="cDate">[16th September 1988]</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="body"><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr1-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Short title</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>1.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;This Act may be cited as the Carriage by Air Act.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr2-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Interpretation</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>2.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Act, unless the context otherwise requires&nbsp;—<table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“court”, in an arbitration allowed by the Warsaw Convention, the Warsaw (Hague) Convention or the Warsaw (Hague) (Montreal) Convention, includes an arbitrator;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Hague Protocol” means the Protocol to amend the Warsaw Convention opened for signature at the Hague on 28th September 1955;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Montreal Protocol No. 4” means Protocol No. 4 to amend the Warsaw (Hague) Convention opened for signature at Montreal on 25th September 1975;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Warsaw Convention” means the original Convention for the unification of certain rules relating to international carriage by air opened for signature at Warsaw on 12th October 1929, the text of which is set out in the Second&nbsp;Schedule;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Warsaw (Hague) Convention” means the Warsaw Convention as amended by the Hague Protocol, the text of which is set out in the First&nbsp;Schedule;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Warsaw (Hague) (Montreal) Convention” means the Warsaw (Hague) Convention as amended by the Montreal Protocol No. 4, the text of which is set out in the Third&nbsp;Schedule.<div class="amendNote">[7/99]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr3-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Conventions to have force of law</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>3.</strong><a name="pr3-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Subject to this Act, the provisions of the Warsaw Convention, the Warsaw (Hague) Convention and the Warsaw (Hague) (Montreal) Convention shall, so far as they relate to the rights and liabilites of carriers, carriers’ employees and agents, passengers, consignors, consignees and other persons, have the force of law in Singapore in relation to any carriage by air to which the Warsaw Convention, the Warsaw (Hague) Convention or the Warsaw (Hague) (Montreal) Convention, as the case may require, applies irrespective of the nationality of the aircraft performing that carriage.<div class="amendNote">[7/99]</div></span><a name="pr3-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;If there is any inconsistency between any of the texts set out in the First, Second and Third Schedules and the authentic text in the French language of the Warsaw Convention, or the Hague Protocol or the Montreal Protocol No. 4, as the case may be, the authentic French text shall prevail.<div class="amendNote">[7/99]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr4-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">High Contracting Parties</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>4.</strong><a name="pr4-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of this Act&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">a High Contracting Party to the Warsaw Convention is a country that has ratified or acceded to that Convention;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">a High Contracting Party to the Warsaw (Hague) Convention is a country that has ratified or acceded to that Convention; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">a High Contracting Party to the Warsaw (Hague) (Montreal) Convention is a country that has ratified or acceded to that Convention,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">except that this Act shall apply to any such High Contracting Party&nbsp;—</td></tr></tbody></table><table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(i)</td><td class="pTxt">only in relation to the territories in respect of which it is a party to the Warsaw Convention, the Warsaw (Hague) Convention or the Warsaw (Hague) (Montreal) Convention, as the case may be; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(ii)</td><td class="pTxt">to the extent that it has availed itself of the provisions of the Additional Protocol at the end of the Warsaw Convention, the Warsaw (Hague) Convention and the Warsaw (Hague) (Montreal) Convention, as the case may be.</td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr4-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Article&nbsp;40A(2) in the First and Third Schedules shall not be read as extending references in those Schedules to the territory of a High Contracting Party (except such as are references to the territory of any State, whether a High Contracting Party or not) to include any territory in respect of which that High Contracting Party is not a party.<div class="amendNote">[41/2007 wef 16/11/2007]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr5-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Fatal accidents</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>5.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;References in section&nbsp;20 of the Civil Law Act (Cap. 43) to a wrongful act, neglect or default shall include references to any occurrence which gives rise to liability under Article&nbsp;17 in the First, Second and Third Schedules.<div class="amendNote">[7/99]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr6-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Limitations of liability</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>6.</strong><a name="pr6-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;It is declared that the limitations on liability in Article&nbsp;22 in the First, Second and Third Schedules shall apply whatever the nature of the proceedings by which liability may be enforced and that, in particular the limitation for each passenger in Article&nbsp;22(1) in the First, Second and Third Schedules shall apply to the aggregate liability of the carrier in all proceedings which may be brought against him under the law of Singapore, together with any proceedings brought against him outside Singapore.<div class="amendNote">[45/98; 7/99]</div></span><a name="pr6-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;A court before which proceedings are brought to enforce a liability which is limited by Article&nbsp;22 in the First, Second or Third Schedule may at any stage of the proceedings make any such order as appears to the court to be just and equitable in view of the provisions of that Article, and of any other proceedings which have been, or are likely to be, commenced in Singapore or elsewhere to enforce the liability in whole or in part.<div
