<div class="front"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="actHd" id="aT-">Constitution of the Republic of Singapore</td></tr></tbody></table><p class="origSrc">(Original Enactment: S 1/63)</p><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="cDate">[9th&nbsp;August 1965]</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="body"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="part" id="P1I-"><div class="partNo">PART I</div><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="partHdr" id="P1I-he-">Preliminary</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr1-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Citation</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>1.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;This Constitution may be cited as the Constitution of the Republic of Singapore.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr2-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Interpretation</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>2.</strong><a name="pr2-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Constitution, unless it is otherwise provided or the context otherwise requires&nbsp;—<table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Cabinet” means the Cabinet constituted under this Constitution;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Civil List” means the provision made under Article&nbsp;22J for the maintenance of the President;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“citizen of Singapore” means any person who, under the provisions of this Constitution, has the status of a citizen of Singapore;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“commencement”, used with reference to this Constitution, means 9th&nbsp;August 1965;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Consolidated Fund” means the Consolidated Fund established by this Constitution;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Council of Presidential Advisers” means the Council of Presidential Advisers constituted under Part&nbsp;VA;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“existing law” means any law having effect as part of the law of Singapore immediately before the commencement of this Constitution;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Government” means the Government of Singapore;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Judge of the Supreme Court” means the Chief Justice, a Judge of Appeal or a Judge of the High Court;<div class="amendNote">[Act 39 of 2014 wef 01/01/2015]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“law” includes written law and any legislation of the United Kingdom or other enactment or instrument whatsoever which is in operation in Singapore and the common law in so far as it is in operation in Singapore and any custom or usage having the force of law in Singapore;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Legal Service Commission” means the Legal Service Commission constituted under this Constitution;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Legislature” means the Legislature of Singapore;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Minister” means a Minister appointed under this Constitution;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“office of profit” means, subject to clause (5), any whole time office in the public service;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Parliament” means the Parliament of Singapore;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“President” means the President of Singapore elected under this Constitution and includes any person for the time being exercising the functions of the office of President;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Presidential Elections Committee” means the Presidential Elections Committee constituted under Article&nbsp;18;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Prime Minister” means the Prime Minister of Singapore appointed under this Constitution;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“public office” means, subject to clause (5), an office of emolument in the public service;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“public officer” means the holder of any public office;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“public seal” means the public seal of Singapore;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“public service” means service under the Government;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Public Service Commission” means the Public Service Commission constituted under this Constitution;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“register of electors” means any register of electors prepared under the provisions of any written law for the time being in force relating to Parliamentary elections;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“remuneration”, in respect of any public officer, means only the emoluments of that officer, the whole or any part of which count for pension or gratuity in accordance with the provisions of any law relating to the grant of pensions or gratuities in respect of the public service;<div class="amendNote">[Act 39 of 2014 wef 01/01/2015]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“reserves”, in relation to the Government, a statutory board or Government company, means the excess of assets over liabilities of the Government, statutory board or Government company, as the case may be;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“session” means the sittings of Parliament commencing when it first meets after being constituted, or after its prorogation or dissolution at any time, and terminating when Parliament is prorogued or is dissolved without having been prorogued;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Singapore” means the Republic of Singapore;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“sitting” means a period during which Parliament is sitting continuously without adjournment, including any period during which Parliament is in committee;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Speaker” and “Deputy Speaker” mean, respectively, the Speaker and a Deputy Speaker of Parliament;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“term of office”, in relation to the Government, means the period&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">commencing on the date the Prime Minister and Ministers first take and subscribe the Oath of Allegiance in accordance with Article&nbsp;27 after a general election; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">ending after the next general election on the date immediately before the Prime Minister and Ministers first take and subscribe the Oath of Allegiance in accordance with Article&nbsp;27;</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“terms of service”, in respect of any officer, includes the remuneration to which that officer is entitled by virtue of his office, and any pension, gratuity or other like allowance payable to or in respect of that officer;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“written law” means this Constitution and all Acts and Ordinances and subsidiary legislation for the time being in force in Singapore.</td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr2-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Except where this Constitution otherwise provides or where the context otherwise requires&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the person or authority having power to make substantive appointments to any public office may appoint a person to perform the functions of that office during any period when it is vacant or when the holder thereof is unable (whether by reason of absence or infirmity of body or mind or any other cause) to perform those functions;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">every appointment to perform the functions of an office made under paragraph&nbsp;(<em>a</em>) shall be made in the same manner as and subject to the same conditions as apply to a substantive appointment to that office;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any reference in this Constitution to the holder of any office by the term designating his office shall be construed as including a reference to any person for the time being lawfully performing the functions of that office; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>d</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any reference in this Constitution to an appointment to any office shall be construed as including a reference to an appointment to perform the functions of that office.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where in this Constitution power is conferred on any person or authority to appoint a person to perform the functions of any office if the holder thereof is unable himself to perform its functions, any such appointment shall not be called in question on the ground that the holder of that office was not unable to perform those functions.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of this Constitution, the resignation of a member of any body or the holder of any office constituted by this Constitution that is required to be addressed to any person shall be deemed to have effect from the time that it is received by that person:<table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="proviso" id="pr2-ps4-vi-"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="provisoText" style="font-size:13pt">Provided that, in the case of a resignation that is required to be addressed to the Speaker, the resignation shall, if the office of Speaker is vacant or the Speaker is absent from Singapore, be deemed to have effect from the time that it is received by a Deputy Speaker on behalf of the Speaker.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of this Constitution, a person shall not be considered as holding a public office or an office of profit by reason of the fact that he is in receipt of any remuneration or allowances (including a pension or other like allowance) in respect of his tenure of the office of President, Prime Minister, Chief Justice, Speaker, Deputy Speaker, Minister, Parliamentary Secretary, Political Secretary, Member of Parliament, Ambassador, High Commissioner or such other office as the President may, from time to time, by order, prescribe<sup>*</sup>.<table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="FN"><sup>*&nbsp;&nbsp;</sup>Offices of Consul-General and Consul have been prescribed by the President — <em>See</em> G.N. No. S 212/72</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps6-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(6)&nbsp;&nbsp;<a name="pr2-ps6-p1a-"></a>(<em>a</em>)&nbsp;&nbsp;Without prejudice to clause (2) when the holder of any public office is on leave of absence pending relinquishment of that office, the person or authority having power to make appointments to that office may appoint another person thereto.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-psb-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(<em>b</em>)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where 2 or more persons are holding the same office by reason of an appointment made pursuant to paragraph&nbsp;(<em>a</em>), the person last appointed shall, in respect of any function conferred on the holder of that office, be deemed to be the sole holder of that office.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps7-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(7)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where a person is required by this Constitution to take an oath, he shall be permitted, if he so desires, to comply with that requirement by making an affirmation.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps8-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(8)&nbsp;&nbsp;References in this Constitution to any period shall, so far as the context admits, be construed as including references to a period beginning before the commencement of this Constitution.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps9-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(9)&nbsp;&nbsp;Subject to this Article, the Interpretation Act (Cap.&nbsp;1) shall apply for the purpose of interpreting this Constitution and otherwise in relation thereto as it applies for the purpose of interpreting and otherwise in relation to any written law within the meaning of that Act.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps10-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(10)&nbsp;&nbsp;Unless the context otherwise requires, any reference in this Constitution to a specified Part, Article or Schedule is a reference to that Part or Article of, or that Schedule to, this Constitution; any reference to a specified chapter, clause, section or paragraph is a reference to that chapter of the Part, that clause of the Article, that section of the&nbsp;Schedule, or that paragraph of the clause or section, in which the reference occurs; and any reference to a group of Articles, sections or divisions of Articles or sections shall be construed as including both the first and the last member of the group referred to.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="part" id="P1II-"><div class="partNo">PART II</div><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="partHdr" id="P1II-he-">The Republic and the Constitution</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr3-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Republic of Singapore</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><sup>*</sup><strong>3.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Singapore shall be a sovereign republic to be known as the Republic of Singapore.</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="FN"><sup>*&nbsp;&nbsp;</sup>Section&nbsp;2(1)(<em>d</em>), Constitution (Amendment) Act 1965 (No. 8 of 1965) and the Republic of Singapore Independence Act 1965 (No. 9 of 1965).</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr4-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Supremacy of Constitution</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>4.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;This Constitution is the supreme law of the Republic of Singapore and any law enacted by the Legislature after the commencement of this Constitution which is inconsistent with this Constitution shall, to the extent of the inconsistency, be void.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr5-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Amendment of Constitution </span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>5.</strong><a name="pr5-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Subject to this Article and Article 8, the provisions of this Constitution may be amended by a law enacted by the Legislature.</span><a name="pr5-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;A Bill seeking to amend any provision in this Constitution shall not be passed by Parliament unless it has been supported on Second and Third Readings by the votes of not less than two-thirds of the total number of Members of Parliament (excluding nominated Members).<div class="amendNote">[Act 28 of 2016 wef 01/04/2017]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt" id="pr5-ps2A-">(2A)&nbsp;&nbsp;[<em>The not in-force clause (2A) was deleted by Act 28 of 2016 wef 01/04/2017</em>]</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr5-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Article, “amendment” includes addition and repeal.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1Rep" id="pr5A-"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1RepText"><strong>5A.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;[<em>The not in-force Article 5A was repealed by Act 28 of 2016 wef 01/04/2017</em>]</td></tr></tbody></table></div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="part" id="P1III-"><div class="partNo">PART III</div><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="partHdr" id="P1III-he-">Protection of the Sovereignty of the Republic of Singapore</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr6-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">No surrender of sovereignty or relinquishment of control over the Police Force or the Armed Forces except by referendum</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>6.</strong><a name="pr6-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;There shall be&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">no surrender or transfer, either wholly or in part, of the sovereignty of the Republic of Singapore as an independent nation, whether by way of merger or incorporation with any other sovereign state or with any Federation, Confederation, country or territory or in any other manner whatsoever; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">no relinquishment of control over the Singapore Police Force or the Singapore Armed Forces,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">unless such surrender, transfer or relinquishment has been supported, at a national referendum, by not less than two-thirds of the total number of votes cast by the electors registered under the Parliamentary Elections Act (Cap.&nbsp;218).</td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr6-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of this Article&nbsp;—<table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Singapore Armed Forces” means the Singapore Armed Forces raised and maintained under the Singapore Armed Forces Act (Cap.&nbsp;295), and includes any civil defence force formed under the Civil Defence Act (Cap.&nbsp;42) and such other force as the President may, by notification in the <em>Gazette</em>, declare to be an armed force for the purposes of this Article;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Singapore Police Force” means the Singapore Police Force and the Special Constabulary established under the Police Force Act (Cap.&nbsp;235) and any Auxiliary Police Force created in accordance with Part&nbsp;IX of that Act, and includes the Vigilante Corps established under the Vigilante Corps Act (Cap.&nbsp;343) and such other force as the President may, by notification in the <em>Gazette</em>, declare to be a police force for the purposes of this Article.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr7-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Participation in co-operative international schemes which are beneficial to Singapore </span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>7.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Without in any way derogating from the force and effect of Article&nbsp;6, nothing in that Article shall be construed as precluding Singapore or any association, body or organisation therein from&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">participating or co-operating in, or contributing towards, any scheme, venture, project, enterprise or undertaking of whatsoever nature, in conjunction or in concert with any other sovereign state or with any Federation, Confederation, country or countries or any association, body or organisation therein, where such scheme, venture, project, enterprise or undertaking confers, has the effect of conferring or is intended to confer, on Singapore or any association, body or organisation therein, any economic, financial, industrial, social, cultural, educational or other benefit of any kind or is, or appears to be, advantageous in any way to Singapore or any association, body or organisation therein; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">entering into any treaty, agreement, contract, pact or other arrangement with any other sovereign state or with any Federation, Confederation, country or countries or any association, body or organisation therein, where such treaty, agreement, contract, pact or arrangement provides for mutual or collective security or any other object or purpose whatsoever which is, or appears to be, beneficial or advantageous to Singapore in any way.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr8-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">No amendment to this Part except by referendum</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>8.</strong><a name="pr8-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;A Bill for making an amendment to this Part shall not be passed by Parliament unless it has been supported, at a national referendum, by not less than two-thirds of the total number of votes cast by the electors registered under the Parliamentary Elections Act (Cap.&nbsp;218).</span><a name="pr8-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Article, “amendment” includes addition and repeal. </td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="part" id="P1IV-"><div class="partNo">PART IV</div><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="partHdr" id="P1IV-he-">Fundamental Liberties</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr9-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Liberty of the person</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>9.</strong><a name="pr9-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;No person shall be deprived of his life or personal liberty save in accordance with law.</span><a name="pr9-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where a complaint is made to the High Court or any Judge thereof that a person is being unlawfully detained, the Court shall inquire into the complaint and, unless satisfied that the detention is lawful, shall order him to be produced before the Court and release him.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr9-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where a person is arrested, he shall be informed as soon as may be of the grounds of his arrest and shall be allowed to consult and be defended by a legal practitioner of his choice.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr9-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where a person is arrested and not released, he shall, without unreasonable delay, and in any case within 48 hours (excluding the time of any necessary journey), be produced before a Magistrate, in person or by way of video-conferencing link (or other similar technology) in accordance with law, and shall not be further detained in custody without the Magistrate’s authority.<div class="amendNote">[9/2010 wef 01/07/2010]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr9-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;Clauses (3) and (4) shall not apply to an enemy alien or to any person arrested for contempt of Parliament pursuant to a warrant issued under the hand of the Speaker.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr9-ps6-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(6)&nbsp;&nbsp;Nothing in this Article shall invalidate any law&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">in force before the commencement of this Constitution which authorises the arrest and detention of any person in the interests of public safety, peace and good order; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">relating to the misuse of drugs or intoxicating substances which authorises the arrest and detention of any person for the purpose of treatment and rehabilitation,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">by reason of such law being inconsistent with clauses (3) and (4), and, in particular, nothing in this Article shall affect the validity or operation of any such law before 10th&nbsp;March 1978.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr10-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Slavery and forced labour prohibited</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>10.</strong><a name="pr10-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;No person shall be held in slavery.</span><a name="pr10-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;All forms of forced labour are prohibited, but Parliament may by law provide for compulsory service for national purposes.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr10-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Work incidental to the serving of a sentence of imprisonment imposed by a court of law shall not be taken to be forced labour within the meaning of this Article.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr11-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Protection against retrospective criminal laws and repeated trials</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>11.</strong><a name="pr11-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;No person shall be punished for an act or omission which was not punishable by law when it was done or made, and no person shall suffer greater punishment for an offence than was prescribed by law at the time it was committed.</span><a name="pr11-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;A person who has been convicted or acquitted of an offence shall not be tried again for the same offence except where the conviction or acquittal has been quashed and a retrial ordered by a court superior to that by which he was convicted or acquitted.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr12-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Equal protection</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>12.</strong><a name="pr12-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;All persons are equal before the law and entitled to the equal protection of the law.</span><a name="pr12-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Except as expressly authorised by this Constitution, there shall be no discrimination against citizens of Singapore on the ground only of religion, race, descent or place of birth in any law or in the appointment to any office or employment under a public authority or in the administration of any law relating to the acquisition, holding or disposition of property or the establishing or carrying on of any trade, business, profession, vocation or employment.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr12-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;This Article does not invalidate or prohibit&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any provision regulating personal law; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any provision or practice restricting office or employment connected with the affairs of any religion, or of an institution managed by a group professing any religion, to persons professing that religion.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr13-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Prohibition of banishment and freedom of movement</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>13.</strong><a name="pr13-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;No citizen of Singapore shall be banished or excluded from Singapore.</span><a name="pr13-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Subject to any law relating to the security of Singapore or any part thereof, public order, public health or the punishment of offenders, every citizen of Singapore has the right to move freely throughout Singapore and to reside in any part thereof.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr14-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Freedom of speech, assembly and association</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>14.</strong><a name="pr14-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Subject to clauses (2) and (3)&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">every citizen of Singapore has the right to freedom of speech and expression;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">all citizens of Singapore have the right to assemble peaceably and without arms; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">all citizens of Singapore have the right to form associations.</td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr14-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Parliament may by law impose&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">on the rights conferred by clause (1)(<em>a</em>), such restrictions as it considers necessary or expedient in the interest of the security of Singapore or any part thereof, friendly relations with other countries, public order or morality and restrictions designed to protect the privileges of Parliament or to provide against contempt of court, defamation or incitement to any offence;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">on the right conferred by clause (1)(<em>b</em>), such restrictions as it considers necessary or expedient in the interest of the security of Singapore or any part thereof or public order; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">on the right conferred by clause (1)(<em>c</em>), such restrictions as it considers necessary or expedient in the interest of the security of Singapore or any part thereof, public order or morality.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr14-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Restrictions on the right to form associations conferred by clause (1) (<em>c</em>) may also be imposed by any law relating to labour or education.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr15-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Freedom of religion</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>15.</strong><a name="pr15-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Every person has the right to profess and practise his religion and to propagate it.</span><a name="pr15-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;No person shall be compelled to pay any tax the proceeds of which are specially allocated in whole or in part for the purposes of a religion other than his own.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr15-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Every religious group has the right&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to manage its own religious affairs;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to establish and maintain institutions for religious or charitable purposes; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to acquire and own property and hold and administer it in accordance with law.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr15-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;This Article does not authorise any act contrary to any general law relating to public order, public health or morality.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr16-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Rights in respect of education</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>16.</strong><a name="pr16-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Without prejudice to the generality of Article&nbsp;12, there shall be no discrimination against any citizen of Singapore on the grounds only of religion, race, descent or place of birth&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">in the administration of any educational institution maintained by a public authority, and, in particular, the admission of pupils or students or the payment of fees; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">in providing out of the funds of a public authority financial aid for the maintenance or education of pupils or students in any educational institution (whether or not maintained by a public authority and whether within or outside Singapore).</td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr16-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Every religious group has the right to establish and maintain institutions for the education of children and provide therein instruction in its own religion, and there shall be no discrimination on the ground only of religion in any law relating to such institutions or in the administration of any such law.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr16-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;No person shall be required to receive instruction in or to take part in any ceremony or act of worship of a religion other than his own.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr16-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of clause (3), the religion of a person under the age of 18 years shall be decided by his parent or guardian.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div></td></tr></tbody></table><div class="ajax-loading">&nbsp;</div><div class="dms" data-field="seriesId" data-term="30c34793-8033-46a5-b6c2-6e239db14cb3"></div><div class="dms" data-field="seriesId" data-term="d9cc4629-991b-4fa5-8168-805ee13340ed"></div><div class="dms" data-field="seriesId" <div class="front"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="actHd" id="aT-">Debtors Act</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="chapNo">(CHAPTER 73)</td></tr></tbody></table><p class="origSrc">(Original Enactment: Ordinance 16 of 1923)</p><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdHdr">REVISED EDITION 2014</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdTxt">(30th June 2014)</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="longTitle" id="al-">An Act relating to debtors and to provide penalties for fraudulent debtors.</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="cDate">[1st January 1935]</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="body"><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr1-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Short title</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>1.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;This Act may be cited as the Debtors Act.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr2-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Interpretation</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>2.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Act, unless there is anything repugnant in the context&nbsp;—<table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“court” means the High Court or a judge when sitting in open court in all cases where proceedings are taken in the High Court and means the District Court or a District Judge when sitting in open court, in all cases where proceedings are taken in a District Court;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“judge” means a judge sitting in chambers in all cases where proceedings are taken in the High Court and means a District Judge sitting in chambers in all cases where proceedings are taken in a District Court;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“judgment” includes any order for the payment of money.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="part" id="P1I-"><div class="partNo">PART I</div><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="partHdr" id="P1I-he-">ARREST, EXAMINATION AND IMPRISONMENT OF JUDGMENT DEBTORS</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr3-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Arrest of judgment debtor</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>3.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Where a judgment for the payment of money remains wholly or in part unsatisfied, whether or not a writ of execution has issued, the court or a judge may order the debtor to be arrested and brought before the court forthwith for examination as hereinafter provided, if it appears to the court or judge that there is probable reason for believing, having regard to his conduct, or the state of his affairs, or otherwise, that he is likely to leave Singapore with a view to avoiding payment of such money or to avoiding examination in respect of his affairs.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr4-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Examination of debtor</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>4.</strong><a name="pr4-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;The examination referred to in section&nbsp;3 shall be an oral examination of the debtor before the court respecting his ability to pay or satisfy the judgment or so much thereof as remains due, and shall be conducted in the manner and subject to any rules for the time being prescribed for the examination of a debtor by way of discovery in aid of execution or under section&nbsp;25.</span><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr4-ps2-"><span class=""><em>Adjournment of examination and security for further attendance</em></span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;If the examination is adjourned, the court may order the debtor to be committed to the civil prison until the adjourned hearing, or until such time as he furnishes security in an amount to be named in the order for his appearance at the adjourned hearing.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr5-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Interim order for protection of debtor’s property</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>5.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;The court may, upon an examination under this Part, make any interim order which it may consider expedient for the protection of any property appearing likely to be available for the discharge of the judgment debt.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr6-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Powers of court on examination</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>6.</strong><a name="pr6-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;On the conclusion of the examination, the court may commit the debtor to the civil prison for a term which may extend to 6&nbsp;weeks or until earlier payment of the judgment debt, or may order that the judgment debt be paid by instalments of such amount and at such times as it thinks fit.</span><a name="pr6-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Subject to any rules of court made under or having effect by virtue of the Supreme Court of Judicature Act (Cap. 322), an order for the payment of instalments under this section shall not be a bar to proceedings in execution unless and except to the extent that the court so directs. </td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr6-ps3-"><span class=""><em>Failure to comply with order for instalments</em></span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;If the debtor makes default in the payment of any instalment ordered to be paid under subsection (1), the judgment creditor may apply in such manner as may be prescribed by rules of court made under or having effect by virtue of the Supreme Court of Judicature Act for a notice in the prescribed form, to be issued from the court office, calling upon the debtor to attend before the court at a time named in the notice, and to show cause why he should not be committed to prison for such default and may cause such notice to be served personally upon him; and if on the day so named, or any subsequent day to which the matter may be adjourned, no sufficient cause is shown by the debtor, the court may commit him to the civil prison for a term which may extend to 6 weeks or until earlier payment of any instalment or instalments due. </td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr6-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;A debtor shall not be committed to prison under this section unless it appears that he has, since the date of the judgment or of the order directing payment by instalments, had sufficient means to pay the judgment or comply with the order, as the case may be.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr7-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Rules</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>7.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Rules of court may be made under the Supreme Court of Judicature Act for the following purposes:<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to require the deposit by the person at whose instance any order for arrest or imprisonment is issued, of a sum of money to provide for the expense of bringing the debtor before the court and the subsistence of the debtor while in prison;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to regulate any matter incidental to such deposit.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr8-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Arrest or commitment to be dependent on deposit of expenses</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>8.</strong><a name="pr8-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where under any rules for the time being in force the judgment creditor is required to deposit money to provide for the expense of bringing the debtor before the court, the debtor shall not be arrested until such deposit has been made; and where the judgment creditor is required to deposit money to provide for the subsistence of the debtor while in prison, the order for committal shall not be executed until such deposit has been made.</span><a name="pr8-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where any further deposit is required during any period of imprisonment under this Part, the court or a judge may, if such deposit is not duly made, order that the debtor be discharged from prison.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr9-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Expenses to be judgment debt</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>9.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Unless in any case the court otherwise orders, the costs and expenses of and incidental to the arrest and imprisonment of any judgment debtor under this Act shall be added to the judgment debt and be recoverable accordingly.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr10-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Commitment of defaulting trustee, etc.</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>10.</strong><a name="pr10-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where the court is satisfied that there has been default by a trustee or person acting in a fiduciary capacity in payment into court of any sum in his possession or under his control, the court may commit such trustee or person to prison for a term which may extend to 6&nbsp;months:<table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="proviso" id="pr10-ps1-vi-"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="provisoText" style="font-size:13pt">Provided that no such committal shall be ordered, if it appears to the court that the trustee or person aforesaid has acted innocently in the matter.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr10-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Upon payment of the amount due the prisoner shall be immediately released.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr11-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Discharge or suspension of order</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>11.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;The court or a judge may discharge or vary any order made under this Part, or may suspend its operation.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr12-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Imprisonment not to operate as satisfaction</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>12.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;No imprisonment under this Act shall operate to satisfy or extinguish any debt, or deprive any person of any right to issue execution against the property of the debtor.</td></tr></tbody></table></div></td></tr></tbody></table><div class="ajax-loading">&nbsp;</div><div class="dms" data-field="seriesId" data-term="8ba73317-95da-4459-bb5a-2ea59147ed9b"></div><div class="dms" data-field="seriesId" data-term="d2583b3f-9cba-4687-af39-ef30ccdf3b07"></div><div class="dms" data-field="seriesId" data-term="40d09d69-a5bc-492e-80ce-6fd1b29934ee"></div><div class="dms" data-field="seriesId" data-term="c25357a9-0ecb-4d21-bc72-466b3528b9a7"></div><div class="dms" data-field="seriesId" data-term="4504790f-d043-4cd3-84e6-8b0d949fe5ba"></div></div><div class="tail"><div class="dms" data-field="seriesId" data-term="5638f4a8-4395-43b6-8e67-2bc156cff569"></div></div>
<div class="front"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="actHd" id="aT-">Electronic Transactions Act</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="chapNo">(CHAPTER 88)</td></tr></tbody></table><p class="origSrc">(Original Enactment: Act 16 of 2010)</p><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdHdr">REVISED EDITION 2011</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdTxt">(31st December 2011)</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="longTitle" id="al-">An Act to provide for the security and use of electronic transactions, to implement the United Nations Convention on the Use of Electronic Communications in International Contracts adopted by the General Assembly of the United Nations on 23rd November 2005 and to provide for matters connected therewith.</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="cDate">[1st July 2010]</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="body"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="part" id="P1I-"><div class="partNo">PART I</div><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="partHdr" id="P1I-he-">PRELIMINARY</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr1-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Short title</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>1.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;This Act may be cited as the Electronic Transactions Act.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr2-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Interpretation</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>2.</strong><a name="pr2-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Act, unless the context otherwise requires&nbsp;—<table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“addressee”, in relation to an electronic communication, means a party who is intended by the originator to receive the electronic communication, but does not include a party acting as an intermediary with respect to that electronic communication;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“authorised officer”, in relation to the exercise of any power or performance of any duty under this Act, means a person to whom the exercise of that power or performance of that duty has been delegated under section&nbsp;27;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“automated message system” means a computer program or an electronic or other automated means used to initiate an action or respond to data messages or performances in whole or in part, without review or intervention by a natural person each time an action is initiated or a response is generated by the program or electronic or other means;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“communication” includes any statement, declaration, demand, notice, request, offer or the acceptance of an offer, that the parties are required to make or choose to make in connection with the formation or performance of a contract;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Controller” means the Controller appointed under section&nbsp;27(1) and includes a Deputy or an Assistant Controller appointed under section&nbsp;27(3);</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“electronic” means relating to technology having electrical, digital, magnetic, wireless, optical, electromagnetic or similar capabilities;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“electronic communication” means any communication that the parties make by means of electronic records;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“electronic record” means a record generated, communicated, received or stored by electronic means in an information system or for transmission from one information system to another;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“information” includes data, text, images, sound, codes, computer programs, software and databases;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“information system” means a system for generating, sending, receiving, storing or otherwise processing electronic records;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“originator”, in relation to an electronic communication, means a party by whom, or on whose behalf, the electronic communication has been sent or generated prior to storage, if any, but does not include a party acting as an intermediary with respect to that electronic communication;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“public agency” means a department or ministry of the Government, an Organ of State or a public authority established by or under a public Act;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“record” means information that is inscribed, stored or otherwise fixed on a tangible medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“rule of law” includes written law;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“secure electronic record” means an electronic record that is treated as a secure electronic record by virtue of section&nbsp;17(1) or any other provision of this Act;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“secure electronic signature” means an electronic signature that is treated as a secure electronic signature by virtue of section&nbsp;18 or any other provision of this Act;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“security procedure” means a procedure for the purpose of&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">verifying that an electronic record is that of a specific person; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">detecting error or alteration in the communication, content or storage of an electronic record since a specific point in time,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="defSO" style="font-size:13pt">which may require the use of algorithms or codes, identifying words or numbers, encryption, answerback or acknowledgment procedures, or similar security devices;</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“signed” or “signature” and its grammatical variations means a method (electronic or otherwise) used to identify a person and to indicate the intention of that person in respect of the information contained in a record;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“specified security procedure” means a security procedure which is specified in the Second&nbsp;Schedule;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“specified security procedure provider” means a person involved in the provision of a specified security procedure.</td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr2-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Act, “place of business”, in relation to a party, means&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any place where the party maintains a non-transitory establishment to pursue an economic activity other than the temporary provision of goods or services out of a specific location; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">if the party is a natural person and he does not have a place of business, the person’s habitual residence.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of subsection&nbsp;(2)&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">if a party has indicated his place of business, the location indicated by him is presumed to be his place of business unless another party proves that the party making the indication does not have a place of business at that location;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">if a party has not indicated a place of business and has more than one place of business, then the place of business is that which has the closest relationship to the relevant contract, having regard to the circumstances known to or contemplated by the parties at any time before or at the conclusion of the contract;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">a location is not a place of business merely because that location is&nbsp;—<table class="p2_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr id="pr2-ps3-p1c-p2i-"><td class="p2No">(i)</td><td class="p2Txt">where equipment and technology supporting an information system used by a party in connection with the formation of a contract are located; or</td></tr><tr id="pr2-ps3-p1c-p2ii-"><td class="p2No">(ii)</td><td class="p2Txt">where the information system may be accessed by other parties; and</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>d</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the sole fact that a party makes use of a domain name or an electronic mail address connected to a specific country does not create a presumption that its place of business is located in that country.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where an electronic communication does not relate to any contract, references to a contract in subsection&nbsp;(3) shall refer to the relevant transaction.<div class="sourceNote">[ETA, ss. 2 and 18(4); UN, Art. 4, 6 and 9(3)(a); US, s. 106(2)]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr3-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Purposes and construction</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>3.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;This Act shall be construed consistently with what is commercially reasonable under the circumstances and to give effect to the following purposes:<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to facilitate electronic communications by means of reliable electronic records;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to facilitate electronic commerce, to eliminate barriers to electronic commerce resulting from uncertainties over writing and signature requirements, and to promote the development of the legal and business infrastructure necessary to implement secure electronic commerce;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to facilitate electronic filing of documents with public agencies, and to promote efficient delivery by public agencies of services by means of reliable electronic records;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>d</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to minimise the incidence of forged electronic records, intentional and unintentional alteration of records, and fraud in electronic commerce and other electronic transactions;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>e</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to help to establish uniformity of rules, regulations and standards regarding the authentication and integrity of electronic records;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>f</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to promote public confidence in the integrity and reliability of electronic records and electronic commerce, and to foster the development of electronic commerce through the use of electronic signatures to lend authenticity and integrity to correspondence in any electronic medium; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>g</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to implement the United Nations Convention on the Use of Electronic Communications in International Contracts adopted by the General Assembly of the United Nations on 23rd November 2005 and to make the law of Singapore on electronic transactions, whether or not involving parties whose places of business are in different States, consistent with the provisions of that Convention.</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="sourceNote">[ETA, s. 3]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr4-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Excluded matters</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>4.</strong><a name="pr4-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;The provisions of this Act specified in the first column of the First&nbsp;Schedule shall not apply to any rule of law requiring writing or signatures in any of the matters specified in the second column of that Schedule.</span><a name="pr4-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Minister may, by order published in the <em>Gazette</em>, amend the First&nbsp;Schedule.<div class="sourceNote">[ETA, s. 4]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr5-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Party autonomy</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>5.</strong><a name="pr5-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Nothing in Part&nbsp;II shall affect any rule of law or obligation requiring the agreement or consent of the parties as to the form of a communication or record, and (unless otherwise agreed or provided by a rule of law) such agreement or consent may be inferred from the conduct of the parties.</span><a name="pr5-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Nothing in Part&nbsp;II shall prevent the parties to a contract or transaction from&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">excluding the use of electronic records, electronic communications or electronic signatures in the contract or transaction by agreement; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">imposing additional requirements as to the form or authentication of the contract or transaction by agreement.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr5-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Subject to any other rights or obligations of the parties to a contract or transaction, the parties may, by agreement&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">exclude section&nbsp;6, 11, 12, 13, 14, 15 or 16 from applying to the contract or transaction; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">derogate from or vary the effect of all or any of those provisions in respect of the contract or transaction.</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="sourceNote">[ETA, s. 5; UN, Art. 3 and 8(2)]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="part" id="P1II-"><div class="partNo">PART II</div><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="partHdr" id="P1II-he-">ELECTRONIC RECORDS, <br>SIGNATURES AND CONTRACTS</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr6-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Legal recognition of electronic records</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>6.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;For the avoidance of doubt, it is declared that information shall not be denied legal effect, validity or enforceability solely on the ground that it is in the form of an electronic record.<div class="sourceNote">[ETA, s. 6; UNCITRAL, Art. 5; UN, Art. 8]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr7-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Requirement for writing</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>7.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Where a rule of law requires information to be written, in writing, to be presented in writing or provides for certain consequences if it is not, an electronic record satisfies that rule of law if the information contained therein is accessible so as to be usable for subsequent reference.<div class="sourceNote">[ETA, s. 7; UNCITRAL, Art. 6; UN, Art. 9(2)]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr8-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Requirement for signature</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>8.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Where a rule of law requires a signature, or provides for certain consequences if a document or a record is not signed, that requirement is satisfied in relation to an electronic record if&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">a method is used to identify the person and to indicate that person’s intention in respect of the information contained in the electronic record; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the method used is either&nbsp;—<table class="p2_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr id="pr8-p1b-p2i-"><td class="p2No">(i)</td><td class="p2Txt">as reliable as appropriate for the purpose for which the electronic record was generated or communicated, in the light of all the circumstances, including any relevant agreement; or</td></tr><tr id="pr8-p1b-p2ii-"><td class="p2No">(ii)</td><td class="p2Txt">proven in fact to have fulfilled the functions described in paragraph&nbsp;(<em>a</em>), by itself or together with further evidence.<div class="sourceNote">[UN, Art. 9(3)]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr9-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Retention of electronic records</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>9.</strong><a name="pr9-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where a rule of law requires any document, record or information to be retained, or provides for certain consequences if it is not, that requirement is satisfied by retaining the document, record or information in the form of an electronic record if the following conditions are satisfied:<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the information contained therein remains accessible so as to be usable for subsequent reference;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the electronic record is retained in the format in which it was originally generated, sent or received, or in a format which can be demonstrated to represent accurately the information originally generated, sent or received;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">such information, if any, as enables the identification of the origin and destination of an electronic record and the date and time when it was sent or received, is retained; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>d</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any additional requirements relating to the retention of such electronic records specified by the public agency which has supervision over the requirement for the retention of such records are complied with.</td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr9-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;An obligation to retain any document, record or information in accordance with subsection&nbsp;(1)(<em>c</em>) shall not extend to any information necessarily and automatically generated solely for the purpose of enabling a record to be sent or received.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr9-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;A person may satisfy the requirement referred to in subsection&nbsp;(1) by using the services of any other person, if the conditions in paragraphs&nbsp;(<em>a</em>) to (<em>d</em>) of that subsection are complied with.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr9-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;Nothing in this section shall apply to&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any rule of law which expressly provides for the retention of documents, records or information in the form of electronic records; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any rule of law requiring that any document, record or information be retained (or which provides for consequences if not) that the Minister, by order published in the <em>Gazette</em>, excludes from the application of this section in respect of such document, record or information.</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="sourceNote">[ETA, s. 9; UNCITRAL, Art. 10]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr10-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Provision of originals</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>10.</strong><a name="pr10-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where a rule of law requires any document, record or information to be provided or retained in its original form, or provides for certain consequences if it is not, that requirement is satisfied by providing or retaining the document, record or information in the form of an electronic record if the following conditions are satisfied:<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">there exists a reliable assurance as to the integrity of the information contained in the electronic record from the time the document, record or information was first made in its final form, whether as a document in writing or as an electronic record;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">where the document, record or information is to be provided to a person, the electronic record that is provided to the person is capable of being displayed to the person; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">any additional requirements relating to the provision or retention of such electronic records specified by the public agency which has supervision over the requirement for the provision or retention of such records are complied with.</td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr10-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of subsection&nbsp;(1)(<em>a</em>)&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the criterion for assessing integrity shall be whether the information has remained complete and unaltered, apart from the introduction of any changes that arise in the normal course of communication, storage and display; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the standard of reliability required shall be assessed in the light of the purpose for which the information was generated and in the light of all the relevant circumstances.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr10-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;A person may satisfy the requirement referred to in subsection&nbsp;(1) by using the services of any other person, if the conditions in paragraphs&nbsp;(<em>a</em>), (<em>b</em>) and (<em>c</em>) of that subsection are complied with.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr10-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;Nothing in this section shall apply to any rule of law requiring that any document, record or information be provided or retained in its original form (or which provides for consequences if not) that the Minister, by order published in the <em>Gazette</em>, excludes from the application of this section in respect of such document, record or information.<div class="sourceNote">[UNCITRAL, Art. 8; UN, Art. 9(4) and (5)]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr11-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Formation and validity of contracts</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>11.</strong><a name="pr11-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the avoidance of doubt, it is declared that in the context of the formation of contracts, an offer and the acceptance of an offer may be expressed by means of electronic communications.</span><a name="pr11-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where an electronic communication is used in the formation of a contract, that contract shall not be denied validity or enforceability solely on the ground that an electronic communication was used for that purpose.<div class="sourceNote">[ETA, s. 11; UNCITRAL, Art. 11(1); UN, Art. 8(1)]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr12-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Effectiveness between parties</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>12.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;As between the originator and the addressee of an electronic communication, a declaration of intent or other statement shall not be denied legal effect, validity or enforceability solely on the ground that it is in the form of an electronic communication.<div class="sourceNote">[ETA, s. 12; UNCITRAL, Art. 12(1)]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr13-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Time and place of despatch and receipt</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>13.</strong><a name="pr13-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;The time of despatch of an electronic communication is&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the time when it leaves an information system under the control of the originator or of the party who sent it on behalf of the originator; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">if the electronic communication has not left an information system under the control of the originator or of the party who sent it on behalf of the originator, the time when the electronic communication is received.</td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr13-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;The time of receipt of an electronic communication is the time when the electronic communication becomes capable of being retrieved by the addressee at an electronic address designated by the addressee.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr13-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;The time of receipt of an electronic communication at an electronic address that has not been designated by the addressee is the time when the electronic communication becomes capable of being retrieved by the addressee at that address and the addressee becomes aware that the electronic communication has been sent to that address.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr13-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of subsection&nbsp;(3), an electronic communication is presumed to be capable of being retrieved by the addressee when it reaches the electronic address of the addressee.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr13-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;An electronic communication is deemed to be despatched at
