<div class="front"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="actHd" id="aT-">State Lands Encroachments Act</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="chapNo">(CHAPTER 315)</td></tr></tbody></table><p class="origSrc">(Original Enactment: Ordinance 10 of 1883)</p><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdHdr">REVISED EDITION 1985</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdTxt">(30th March 1987)</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="longTitle" id="al-">An Act to prevent encroachments upon State lands.</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="cDate">[2nd November 1883]</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="body"><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr1-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Short title</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>1.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;This Act may be cited as the State Lands Encroachments Act.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr2-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Information of encroachment</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>2.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;A Magistrate’s Court, upon the sworn information of the Commissioner of Lands, or of any land revenue or other public officer, charging any person with being in unlawful occupation of any State land, may issue a summons for the appearance before it of that person.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr3-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Removal of unlawful occupants</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>3.</strong><a name="pr3-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Magistrate’s Court shall proceed in a summary way in the presence of the parties, or in case of wilful absence of any person against whom such information has been laid, then in his absence, to hear and determine the information.</span><a name="pr3-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;In any action commenced under section&nbsp;2 for the removal of any person in unlawful occupation of State land, the defendant may within such time as may be prescribed by the Rules of Court for the time being in force, apply to the High Court for the action to be transferred to the High Court on the ground that the defendant is claiming title to the land.<div class="amendNote">[23/74]</div><div class="amendNote">[Act 5 of 2014 wef 07/03/2014]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr3-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;On the hearing of any such application, the High Court, if it is satisfied that a bona fide claim of title is raised, may make an order for the action to be transferred to the High Court.<div class="amendNote">[23/74]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr4-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Warrant issuable by court for dispossession</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>4.</strong><a name="pr4-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Magistrate’s Court on being satisfied of the truth of the information shall issue a warrant addressed to the Commissioner of Police or to any police officer requiring him forthwith to dispossess and remove that person from the land, and on behalf of the State to take possession of the land, together with all crops growing thereon, and all buildings and other immovable property upon and affixed thereto, and all movable property found thereon.<div class="amendNote">[23/74]</div></span><a name="pr4-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;The person to whom the warrant is addressed shall forthwith carry it into execution.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Such warrant shall not issue until a period of 48 hours has elapsed from the time of adjudication.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Government may forfeit any movable property which has been seized on the land pursuant to the execution of a warrant referred to in subsection&nbsp;(1) if such movable property has been seized after the expiry of period of 28 days from the date of service of a written notice on the unlawful occupants of the land requiring them to vacate the land and warning them that if any movable property thereon is not so removed within 28 days of the date of service of the notice that property may be seized and forfeited to the Government. <div class="amendNote">[23/74]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;If the summons is dismissed, the Magistrate’s Court may order payment by the Government to the party against whom it was issued of such sum as the Court considers to be the amount of costs fairly incurred.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr5-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Forms</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>5.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;The information, summons and warrant respectively referred to in sections&nbsp;2 and 4 may be in the forms A, B and C in the&nbsp;Schedule.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr6-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Demolition of unlawful buildings</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>6.</strong><a name="pr6-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;A Magistrate’s Court, upon the sworn information of the Commissioner of Lands, or of any land revenue or other public officer, that any building has been erected or constructed upon State land without lawful authority, shall issue a summons calling upon any person interested to show cause why an order should not be made declaring the building to be State property and authorising its demolition by or under the authority of the Commissioner of Lands, or any land revenue or other public officer.</span><a name="pr6-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;That summons shall forthwith be posted or affixed by a court officer to the building referred to in the summons or as near thereto as may be practicable and no other service of the summons shall be necessary.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr6-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;If no bona fide application to show cause as aforesaid is made to the Magistrate’s Court issuing the summons by any person interested within 3 clear days of the date on which the summons is posted or affixed to the building, then the order shall be made by the Magistrate’s Court and may be enforced forthwith.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr6-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;If an application to show cause as aforesaid and supported by affidavit showing the grounds of the application is made to the Magistrate’s Court issuing the summons by a person interested within the time provided by subsection&nbsp;(3), then the Magistrate’s Court on being satisfied that the application is a bona fide one shall give notice of the application to the person swearing the information, shall fix a date for the hearing and determination of the information and shall give due notice thereof to the parties concerned.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr6-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;On the date so fixed for the hearing and determination of the information, the Magistrate’s Court shall proceed in a summary way in the presence of the parties, or in case of wilful absence of any of the parties, then in his or their absence, to hear and determine the information.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr6-ps6-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(6)&nbsp;&nbsp;The jurisdiction of that Court shall be taken away by a bona fide claim of title raised by a person interested at the hearing.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr6-ps7-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(7)&nbsp;&nbsp;In this section, “building” includes any structure whatsoever.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr6-ps8-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(8)&nbsp;&nbsp;The information and summons referred to in this section may be in the forms D and E in the&nbsp;Schedule.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr7-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Penalties for trespassing</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>7.</strong><a name="pr7-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any person who&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">unlawfully enters into possession of any State land, either by residing or by erecting any building or hut thereon or by clearing, enclosing or cultivating any part thereof;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">unlawfully trespasses on State land by depositing, placing or throwing any article or thing whatsoever, or any waste, refuse or other thing, thereon; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">directly or indirectly abets the commission of such an act or trespass by another person,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">shall be guilty of an offence and shall be liable on conviction to a fine not exceeding $5,000 or to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or to both, and a District Court or a Magistrate’s Court shall have jurisdiction to hear and determine all proceedings under this subsection and, notwithstanding anything to the contrary in the Criminal Procedure Code [Cap. 68], shall have the power to impose the full penalty or punishment provided by this subsection.</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="amendNote">[23/74]</div></span><a name="pr7-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any person who&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">unlawfully enters upon any State land and cuts timber or produce thereon; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">directly or indirectly abets the commission of such an act by another person,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">shall be liable for a first offence to a fine not exceeding $200, and, for a second or subsequent offence, to a fine not exceeding $500 or to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6 months or to both, and a Magistrate’s Court shall have jurisdiction to hear and determine all proceedings under this subsection.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr7-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where an offence under subsection&nbsp;(1) has been committed by a company or an association or body of persons, corporate or unincorporate, any person who at the time of the commission of the offence was a director, manager, partner, secretary or other officer thereof or was purporting to act in such capacity shall also be deemed to be guilty of such offence unless he proves that the offence was committed without his consent or connivance and that he exercised all such diligence to prevent the commission of the offence as he ought to have exercised having regard to the nature of his functions in that capacity and to all the circumstances.<div class="amendNote">[23/74]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr7A-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Defence relying on implied easement of support</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>7A.</strong><a name="pr7A-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;In any proceedings against a person for an offence under section&nbsp;7 for erecting or installing any structure in any subterranean space that is State land, or for maintaining, replacing, renewing or restoring any such structure, it is a defence for the person charged to prove, on a balance of probabilities, that&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the person, or the company or association or body of persons of which the person is a director, manager, partner, secretary or other officer, is entitled to exercise rights under the easement of support implied under section&nbsp;3C of the State Lands Act (Cap.&nbsp;314);</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the erection or installation of the structure, or the maintenance, replacement, renewal or restoration of the structure, as the case may be, is in accordance with section&nbsp;3C of the State Lands Act; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the person, or the company or association or body of persons of which the person is a director, manager, partner, secretary or other officer, is authorised by or under the written law for the time being in force relating to planning and use of land to erect or install the structure, or to maintain, replace, renew or restore the structure, as the case may be.</td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr7A-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;A defence under this section is additional to any other defence available to the defendant apart from this section.<div class="amendNote">[Act 11 of 2015 wef 08/05/2015]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr8-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Recovery of expenses</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>8.</strong><a name="pr8-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;The court before which any person is convicted of an offence under section&nbsp;7 may order that person to pay, in addition to any fine which has been imposed for the offence, the value of any timber or other Government property cut down, destroyed or injured upon the land during any period of the unlawful occupation thereof by that person, and the expense of any survey which has become necessary for proving such unlawful occupation, or for ascertaining the extent thereof.</span><a name="pr8-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purpose of ascertaining such value and expense, a certificate in writing under the hand of the Collector of Land Revenue shall be held, until the contrary is proved, to be proof that the sum therein set down is the true amount to be recovered from that person in respect of the value and expense.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr8-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any sum ordered to be paid under this section, whatever may be the amount thereof, may be recovered in the manner provided for the recovery of fines by the Criminal Procedure Code [Cap.&nbsp;68]. </td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr9-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Forfeiture of abandoned land to State</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>9.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Subject to section&nbsp;10, any land alienated or demised by or on behalf of the State which has been abandoned for 3 years or upwards by the person to whom it was alienated or demised or by any person claiming title through him, shall, notwithstanding that some person may be found in occupation thereof or of any part thereof, be forfeited to the State.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr10-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Procedure for resumption</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>10.</strong><a name="pr10-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;When any land alienated or demised by or on behalf of the Crown or the State appears to the Collector of Land Revenue to have been so abandoned for 3 years or upwards, the Collector may, with the sanction of the Minister, declare by notice in the <em>Gazette</em> and by a notice in the English, Malay, Chinese and Tamil languages posted on the land, that, unless within 6 months a claim to the land or to any interest therein, whether by long possession or otherwise, is established to the satisfaction of the Collector, it shall be deemed to have been forfeited to the State.</span><a name="pr10-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Unless within the term of 6 months so appointed a claim to the land or any interest therein is established as in the notice provided, the land shall be deemed accordingly to have been forfeited to the State, and any grant or lease affecting the land theretofore executed, and any deed purporting to deal with the same, or any part thereof, shall be void.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr10-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Whenever any land is forfeited to the State under this section, a notification to that effect shall be published in the <em>Gazette</em> and shall be posted on the land or at the police station nearest thereto.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr11-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Limitation</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>11.</strong><a name="pr11-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any land forfeited to the State under section&nbsp;10 may be dealt with as seems expedient to the President.</span><a name="pr11-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Such land shall be appraised without delay by some person or persons appointed for that purpose by the Minister, and the appraised value shall be recorded in the records of the Singapore Land Authority.<div class="amendNote">[17/2001 wef 01/06/2001]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr11-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;If, within 6 years from the forfeiture of the land, any person establishes a claim thereto or to any interest therein to the satisfaction of the President, he shall be entitled to receive out of the Consolidated Fund such sum, not exceeding the appraised value of that land so recorded, as the President directs.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr12-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">State land not to be acquired by adverse possession</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>12.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;No State land shall be acquired by possession or unlawful occupation and the provisions of the Limitation Act [Cap. 163] shall not apply to any action brought by the Government for the recovery of State land.<div class="amendNote">[23/74]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr13-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Penalty for depasturing on State land</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>13.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Any person who knowingly and wilfully depastures without authority in that behalf any horse or cattle on any State land, not being a common, shall be guilty of an offence and shall be liable on conviction to a fine not exceeding $500.<div class="amendNote">[23/74]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr14-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Penalty for other trespasses on State land</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>14.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Any person who is not authorised in that behalf cuts, digs or takes from any State land any live or dead timber, or other vegetable product, or any beeswax, guano, mineral, gravel, stone, coral, shell, sand, loam, brick-earth or other product, or cuts, removes or sells any timber or produce lying or being on State land or strips or removes bark from any tree in any State land, shall be guilty of an offence and shall be liable on conviction to a fine not exceeding $2,000.<div class="amendNote">[23/74]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1Rep" id="pr15-"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1RepText"><strong>15.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;[<em>Repealed by Act 15/2010 wef 02/01/2011</em>]</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr16-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Forest rangers and penghulus</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>16.</strong><a name="pr16-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Minister may appoint a sufficient number of persons to be forest rangers and penghulus, and may define the boundaries within which the forest rangers and penghulus shall exercise the functions herein assigned to them.</span><a name="pr16-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Every such forest ranger or penghulu shall, during his continuance in office, do all acts for preventing intrusion, encroachment and trespass on State lands, or for levying or recovering the rent or the licence fee payable in respect thereof, or in respect of the rent of any land held under any grant or lease from the Government, or for taking and recovering possession of any allotment or lands in case of forfeiture, or for such other purpose as the Minister may prescribe.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr17-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Forest rangers and penghulus to give information</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>17.</strong><a name="pr17-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any forest ranger or penghulu who wilfully or knowingly refuses or neglects to give every information within his knowledge or power immediately to the Commissioner of Lands, or to the Collector of Land Revenue, of any encroachment made by any person upon any State land, and situated in the district of that forest ranger or penghulu shall be guilty of an offence and shall be liable on conviction to a fine not exceeding $200.</span><a name="pr17-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any forest ranger, penghulu or police officer who without lawful excuse neglects or refuses to do and perform any of the duties, matters and things imposed on him by this Act shall be guilty of an offence and shall be liable on conviction to a fine not exceeding $200.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr18-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Arrest without warrant</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>18.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;All forest rangers, penghulus and police officers within their respective jurisdictions are hereby required to arrest without warrant and take before a Magistrate any person whom they find committing any offence punishable under section&nbsp;13 or 14.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr19-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Right of proceeding under the law</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>19.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Nothing in this Act shall be held to deprive the Government of any right to proceed under the law, or of any remedy against trespassers given by law.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr20-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Interpretation</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>20.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Act, “State land” includes all land contained or referred to in a notification or declaration made under the provisions of section&nbsp;3 or 5 of the Land Acquisition Act [Cap. 152], and published in the <em>Gazette</em> in accordance with those provisions. </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div class="tail"><div class="ajax-loading">&nbsp;</div><div class="dms" data-field="seriesId" data-term="765718ed-79d2-4907-b85e-4c6df43014b9"></div><div class="dms" data-field="seriesId" data-term="f629ecbf-5084-4229-9386-3cf8b3c8c179"></div></div>
<div class="front"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="actHd" id="aT-">Supply of Goods Act</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="chapNo">(CHAPTER 394)</td></tr></tbody></table><p class="origSrc">(Original Enactment: U.K. 1982, c. 29)</p><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdHdr">REVISED EDITION 1999</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdTxt">(1st August 1999)</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="longTitle" id="al-">An Act to amend the law with respect to the terms to be implied in certain contracts for the transfer of the property in goods and in certain contracts for the hire of goods and for connected purposes.</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="cDate">[12th November 1993<sup>*</sup>]</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="FN"><sup>*&nbsp;&nbsp;</sup> Date when this Act was made applicable by the Application of English Law Act (Cap. 7A).</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="body"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="part" id="P1I-"><div class="partNo">PART I</div><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="sGrpTail" id="P1I-P4_1-"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="partHdrIta"><span style=""></span><span style="">Contracts for Transfer of Property in Goods</span></td></tr></tbody></table><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr1-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">The contracts concerned</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>1.</strong><a name="pr1-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Act, “contract for the transfer of goods” means a contract under which one person transfers or agrees to transfer to another the property in goods, other than an excepted contract.</span><a name="pr1-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of this section, an excepted contract means any of the following:<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">a contract of sale of goods;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">a hire-purchase agreement;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">a transfer or agreement to transfer which is made by deed and for which there is no consideration other than the presumed consideration imported by the deed; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>d</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">a contract intended to operate by way of mortgage, pledge, charge or other security.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr1-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of this Act, a contract is a contract for the transfer of goods whether or not services are also provided or to be provided under the contract, and, subject to subsection&nbsp;(2), whatever is the nature of the consideration for the transfer or agreement to transfer.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr2-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Implied terms about title, etc.</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>2.</strong><a name="pr2-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;In a contract for the transfer of goods, other than one to which subsection&nbsp;(3) applies, there is an implied condition on the part of the transferor that in the case of a transfer of the property in the goods he has a right to transfer the property and in the case of an agreement to transfer the property in the goods he will have such a right at the time when the property is to be transferred.</span><a name="pr2-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;In a contract for the transfer of goods, other than one to which subsection&nbsp;(3) applies, there is also an implied warranty that&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the goods are free, and will remain free until the time when the property is to be transferred, from any charge or encumbrance not disclosed or known to the transferee before the contract is made; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the transferee will enjoy quiet possession of the goods except so far as it may be disturbed by the owner or other person entitled to the benefit of any charge or encumbrance so disclosed or known.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;This subsection applies to a contract for the transfer of goods in the case of which there appears from the contract or is to be inferred from its circumstances an intention that the transferor should transfer only such title as he or a third person may have.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;In a contract to which subsection&nbsp;(3) applies, there is an implied warranty that all charges or encumbrances known to the transferor and not known to the transferee have been disclosed to the transferee before the contract is made.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr2-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;In a contract to which subsection&nbsp;(3) applies, there is also an implied warranty that none of the following will disturb the transferee’s quiet possession of the goods, namely&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the transferor;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">in a case where the parties to the contract intend that the transferor should transfer only such title as a third person may have, that person;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">anyone claiming through or under the transferor or that third person otherwise than under a charge or encumbrance disclosed or known to the transferee before the contract is made.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr3-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Implied terms where transfer is by description</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>3.</strong><a name="pr3-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;This section applies where, under a contract for the transfer of goods, the transferor transfers or agrees to transfer the property in the goods by description.</span><a name="pr3-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;In such case there is an implied condition that the goods will correspond with the description.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr3-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;If the transferor transfers or agrees to transfer the property in the goods by sample as well as by description, it is not sufficient that the bulk of the goods corresponds with the sample if the goods do not also correspond with the description.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr3-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;A contract is not prevented from falling within subsection&nbsp;(1) by reason only that, being exposed for supply, the goods are selected by the transferee.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr4-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Implied terms about quality or fitness</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>4.</strong><a name="pr4-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Except as provided by this section and section&nbsp;5 and subject to the provisions of any other enactment, there is no implied condition or warranty about the quality or fitness for any particular purpose of goods supplied under a contract for the transfer of goods.</span><a name="pr4-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where, under such a contract, the transferor transfers the property in goods in the course of a business, there is an implied condition that the goods supplied under the contract are of satisfactory quality.<div class="amendNote">[44/96]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps2A-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2A)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of this section and section&nbsp;5, goods are of satisfactory quality if they meet the standard that a reasonable person would regard as satisfactory, taking account of any description of the goods, the price (if relevant) and all the other relevant circumstances.<div class="amendNote">[44/96]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;The condition implied by subsection&nbsp;(2) does not extend to any matter making the quality of goods unsatisfactory&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">which is specifically drawn to the transferee’s attention before the contract is made;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">where the transferee examines the goods before the contract is made, which that examination ought to reveal; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">where the property in the goods is transferred by reference to a sample, which would have been apparent on a reasonable examination of the sample.<div class="amendNote">[44/96]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;Subsection&nbsp;(5) applies where, under a contract for the transfer of goods, the transferor transfers the property in goods in the course of a business and the transferee, expressly or by implication, makes known&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to the transferor; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">where the consideration or part of the consideration for the transfer is a sum payable by instalments and the goods were previously sold by a credit-broker to the transferor, to that credit-broker,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">any particular purpose for which the goods are being acquired.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;In that case there is, subject to subsection&nbsp;(6), an implied condition that the goods supplied under the contract are reasonably fit for that purpose, whether or not that is a purpose for which such goods are commonly supplied.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps6-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(6)&nbsp;&nbsp;Subsection&nbsp;(5) does not apply where the circumstances show that the transferee does not rely, or that it is unreasonable for him to rely, on the skill or judgment of the transferor or credit-broker.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps7-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(7)&nbsp;&nbsp;An implied condition or warranty about quality or fitness for a particular purpose may be annexed by usage to a contract for the transfer of goods.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps8-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(8)&nbsp;&nbsp;The preceding provisions of this section apply to a transfer by a person who in the course of a business is acting as agent for another as they apply to a transfer by a principal in the course of a business, except where that other is not transferring in the course of a business and either the transferee knows that fact or reasonable steps are taken to bring it to the transferee’s notice before the contract concerned is made.</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt" id="pr4-ps9-">(9)&nbsp;&nbsp;[<em>Deleted by Act 44/96</em>]</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr5-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Implied terms where transfer is by sample</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>5.</strong><a name="pr5-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;This section applies where, under a contract for the transfer of goods, the transferor transfers or agrees to transfer the property in the goods by reference to a sample.</span><a name="pr5-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;In such a case, there is an implied condition&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">that the bulk will correspond with the sample in quality;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">that the transferee will have a reasonable opportunity of comparing the bulk with the sample; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">that the goods will be free from any defect, making their quality unsatisfactory, which would not be apparent on reasonable examination of the sample.<div class="amendNote">[44/96]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt" id="pr5-ps3-">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;[<em>Deleted by Act 44/96</em>]</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr5-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of this section, a transferor transfers or agrees to transfer the property in goods by reference to a sample where there is an express or implied term to that effect in the contract concerned.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr5A-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Modification of remedies for breach of statutory condition in non-consumer contracts for transfer of goods</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>5A.</strong><a name="pr5A-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where in the case of a contract for the transfer of goods&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the transferee would, apart from this subsection, have the right to treat the contract as repudiated by reason of a breach on the part of the transferor of a condition implied by section&nbsp;3, 4 or 5(2)(<em>a</em>) or (<em>c</em>); but</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the breach is so slight that it would be unreasonable for the transferee to do so,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">then, if the transferee does not deal as consumer, the breach is not to be treated as a breach of condition but may be treated as a breach of warranty.</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="amendNote">[44/96]</div></span><a name="pr5A-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;This section applies unless a contrary intention appears in, or is to be implied from, the contract.<div class="amendNote">[44/96]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr5A-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;It is for the transferor to show that a breach fell within subsection&nbsp;(1)(<em>b</em>).<div class="amendNote">[44/96]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="sGrpTail" id="P1I-P4_6-"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="partHdrIta"><span style=""></span><span style="">Contracts for hire of goods</span></td></tr></tbody></table><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr6-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">The contracts concerned</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>6.</strong><a name="pr6-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Act, “contract for the hire of goods” means a contract under which one person bails or agrees to bail goods to another by way of hire, other than a hire-purchase agreement.</span><a name="pr6-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of this Act, a contract is a contract for the hire of goods whether or not services are also provided or to be provided under the contract, and whatever is the nature of the consideration for the bailment or agreement to bail by way of hire.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr7-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Implied terms about right to transfer possession, etc.</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>7.</strong><a name="pr7-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;In a contract for the hire of goods, there is an implied condition on the part of the bailor that in the case of a bailment he has a right to transfer possession of the goods by way of hire for the period of the bailment and in the case of an agreement to bail he will have such a right at the time of the bailment.</span><a name="pr7-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;In a contract for the hire of goods, there is also an implied warranty that the bailee will enjoy quiet possession of the goods for the period of the bailment except so far as the possession may be disturbed by the owner or other person entitled to the benefit of any charge or encumbrance disclosed or known to the bailee before the contract is made.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr7-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;This section does not affect the right of the bailor to repossess the goods under an express or implied term of the contract.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr8-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Implied terms where hire is by description</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>8.</strong><a name="pr8-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;This section applies where, under a contract for the hire of goods, the bailor bails or agrees to bail the goods by description.</span><a name="pr8-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;In such a case, there is an implied condition that the goods will correspond with the description.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr8-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;If under the contract the bailor bails or agrees to bail the goods by reference to a sample as well as a description, it is not sufficient that the bulk of the goods corresponds with the sample if the goods do not also correspond with the description.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr8-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;A contract is not prevented from falling within subsection&nbsp;(1) by reason only that, being exposed for supply, the goods are selected by the bailee.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr9-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Implied terms about quality or fitness</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>9.</strong><a name="pr9-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Except as provided by this section and section&nbsp;10 and subject to the provisions of any other enactment, there is no implied condition or warranty about the quality or fitness for any particular purpose of goods bailed under a contract for the hire of goods.</span><a name="pr9-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where, under such a contract, the bailor bails goods in the course of a business, there is an implied condition that the goods supplied under the contract are of satisfactory quality.<div class="amendNote">[44/96]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr9-ps2A-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2A)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of this section and section&nbsp;10, goods are of satisfactory quality if they meet the standard that a reasonable person would regard as satisfactory, taking account of any description of the goods, the consideration for the bailment (if relevant) and all the other relevant circumstances.<div class="amendNote">[44/96]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr9-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;The condition implied by subsection&nbsp;(2) does not extend to any matter making the quality of goods unsatisfactory&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">which is specifically drawn to the bailee’s attention before the contract is made;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">where the bailee examines the goods before the contract is made, which that examination ought to reveal; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">where the goods are bailed by reference to a sample, which would have been apparent on a reasonable examination of the sample.<div class="amendNote">[44/96]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr9-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;Subsection&nbsp;(5) applies where, under a contract for the hire of goods, the bailor bails goods in the course of a business and the bailee, expressly or by implication, makes known&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to the bailor in the course of negotiations conducted by him in relation to the making of the contract; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">to a credit-broker in the course of negotiations conducted by that broker in relation to goods sold by him to the bailor before forming the subject-matter of the contract,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1N2SO" style="font-size:13pt">any particular purpose for which the goods are being bailed.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr9-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;In that case there is, subject to subsection&nbsp;(6), an implied condition that the goods supplied under the contract are reasonably fit for that purpose, whether or not that is a purpose for which such goods are commonly supplied.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr9-ps6-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(6)&nbsp;&nbsp;Subsection&nbsp;(5) does not apply where the circumstances show that the bailee does not rely, or that it is unreasonable for him to rely, on the skill or judgment of the bailor or credit-broker.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr9-ps7-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(7)&nbsp;&nbsp;An implied condition or warranty about quality or fitness for a particular purpose may be annexed by usage to a contract for the hire of goods.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr9-ps8-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(8)&nbsp;&nbsp;The preceding provisions of this section apply to a bailment by a person who in the course of a business is acting as agent for another as they apply to a bailment by a principal in the course of a business, except where that other is not bailing in the course of a business and either the bailee knows that fact or reasonable steps are taken to bring it to the bailee’s notice before the contract concerned is made.</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt" id="pr9-ps9-">(9)&nbsp;&nbsp;[<em>Deleted by Act 44/96</em>]</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr10-"><span class="noBold"></span><span name="pr10-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;In such a case, there is an implied condition&nbsp;—<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;For the purposes of this section, a bailor bails or agrees to bail goods by reference to a sample where there is an express or implied term to that effect in the contract concerned.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr10A-"><span class="noBold"></span><span style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the bailee would, apart from this subsection, have the right to treat the contract as repudiated by within subsection&nbsp;(1)(<em>b</em>).<div class="amendNote">[44/96]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="sGrpTail" id="P1I-P4_11-"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="partHdrIta"><span style=""></span><span style="">Exclusion of implied terms, etc.</span></td></tr></tbody></table><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr11-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Exclusion of implied terms, etc.</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>11.</strong><a name="pr11-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where a right, duty or liability would arise under a contract for the transfer of goods or a contract for the hire of goods by implication of law, it may (subject to subsection&nbsp;(2) and the Unfair Contract Terms Act) (Cap. 396) be negatived or varied by express agreement, or by the course of dealing between the parties, or by such usage as binds both parties to the contract.</span><a name="pr11-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;An express condition or warranty does not negative a condition or warranty implied by the preceding provisions of this Act unless inconsistent with it.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr11-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;Nothing in the preceding provisions of this Act prejudices the operation of any other enactment or any rule of law whereby any condition or warranty (other than one relating to quality or fitness) is to be implied in a contract for the transfer of goods or a contract for the hire of goods.</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><div class="ajax-loading">&nbsp;</div><div class="dms" data-field="seriesId" 336)</td></tr></tbody></table><p class="origSrc">(Original Enactment: Act 11 of 2005)</p><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdHdr">REVISED EDITION 2006</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdTxt">(31st July 2006)</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="longTitle" id="al-">An Act to provide for the licensing and regulation of trust companies and for matters connected therewith.</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="cDate">[1st February 2006]</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="body"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="part" id="P1I-"><div class="partNo">PART I</div><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="partHdr" id="P1I-he-">PRELIMINARY</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr1-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Short title</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>1.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;This Act may be cited as the Trust Companies Act.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr2-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Interpretation</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>2.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Act, unless the context otherwise requires&nbsp;—<table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“advocate and solicitor” means an advocate and solicitor of the Supreme Court or a foreign lawyer as defined in the same meaning as in section 2(1) of the Securities and Futures Act (Cap. 289);<div class="amendNote">[Act 4 of 2017 wef 08/10/2018]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“chief executive”, in relation to a licensed trust company, means any person, by whatever name described, who —<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" 18/04/2013]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“collective investment scheme” has the same meaning as in section&nbsp;16(3);</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“corporation” has the same meaning as in section&nbsp;4(1) of the Companies Act (Cap. 50);</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“director” has the same meaning as in section&nbsp;4(1) of the Companies Act;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“executive officer”, in relation to a licensed trust company, means any person, by whatever name described, who —<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">is in the direct employment of, or acting for or by arrangement with, the licensed trust company; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">is concerned with or takes part in the management of the licensed trust company width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“financial year” has the same meaning as in section&nbsp;4(1) of the Companies Act (Cap.&nbsp;50);<div class="amendNote">[2/2007 wef 01/03/2007]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“futures contract” has the same meaning as in section&nbsp;2(1) of the Securities and Futures Act (Cap. 289);</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“licensed trust company” means a corporation holding a trust business licence;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“officer” has the same meaning as in section&nbsp;4(1) of the Companies Act;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“parent supervisory authority”, in relation to a licensed trust company incorporated outside Singapore, means the supervisory authority which is responsible, under the laws of the country or territory where the licensed trust company is incorporated, formed or established, for supervising the licensed trust company;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“protected party”, in relation to a trust company, means a trust for which the trust company provides trust business services and includes the settlor and beneficiary under the trust;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“resident manager” means an individual resident in Singapore who, under the immediate authority of the directors of a licensed trust company, is responsible for the conduct of the trust business of the licensed trust company;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“securities” has the same meaning as in section&nbsp;2(1) of the Securities and Futures Act (Cap. 289);</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“specified securities-based derivatives contract” has the same meaning as in section 2(1) of the Securities and Futures Act;<div class="amendNote">[Act 4 of 2017 wef 08/10/2018]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“trust business” means any business specified in the First&nbsp;Schedule;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td business;</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“trust business service” means any service in respect of any business specified in the <div class="front"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="actHd" id="aT-">Wildlife Act</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="chapNo">(CHAPTER 351)</td></tr></tbody></table><p class="origSrc">(Original Enactment: Ordinance 5 of 1965)</p><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdHdr">REVISED EDITION 2000</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="revdTxt">(30th December 2000)</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="longTitle" id="al-">An Act for the protection, preservation and management of wildlife for the purposes of maintaining a healthy ecosystem and safeguarding public safety and health, and for related matters.<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="cDate">[22nd October 1965]</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="body"><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr1-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Short title</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>1.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;This Act may be cited as the Wildlife Act.<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr2-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Interpretation</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>2.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;In this Act, unless the context otherwise requires&nbsp;—<table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“animal” includes any mammal, bird, reptile, amphibian, fish or invertebrate, whether of a wild nature or otherwise;<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“animal-related business” means —<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">the operation of any place or establishment for the purpose of —<table class="p2_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr id="pr2-pdanimalrelatedbusiness-p1a-p2i-"><td class="p2No">(i)</td><td class="p2Txt">using or holding animals for display, sport, entertainment, sale, breeding or conservation; or</td></tr><tr id="pr2-pdanimalrelatedbusiness-p1a-p2ii-"><td class="p2No">(ii)</td><td class="p2Txt">the care, boarding, grooming, treatment, vaccination, inoculation, training or destruction of animals, for reward;</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">the provision of any service relating to the care, boarding, grooming, treatment, vaccination, inoculation, training, transportation, capture or destruction of animals, for reward; or</td></tr><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">the operation of any animal rescue or welfare organisation or facility,</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="defSO" style="font-size:13pt">but does not include any business in respect of animals intended for consumption;</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“authorised officer” means any person appointed under section&nbsp;4(2) by the Director-General to be an authorised officer;</td></tr></tbody></table><span id="pr2-pd-oc1-"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="definitionRepealed">[<em>Deleted by Act 10 of 2019 wef 01/04/2019</em>]</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Board” means the National Parks Board established by the repealed National Parks Act (Cap.&nbsp;198A, 1991&nbsp;Ed.) as in force before 1 July 1996 and continued by section&nbsp;3 of the National Parks Board Act (Cap.&nbsp;198A);<div class="amendNote">[Act 10 of 2019 wef 01/04/2019]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“conveyance” includes any vehicle, vessel, train, aircraft or other mode of transport;<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“Director-General” means the Director-General, Wildlife Management appointed under section&nbsp;4(1);<div class="amendNote">[Act 10 of 2019 wef 01/04/2019]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><span id="pr2-pd-oc2-"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="definitionRepealed">[<em>Deleted by Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020</em>]</td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“enforcement officer” means an authorised officer, a police officer or an officer of customs;<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“limited liability partnership” has the meaning given by the Limited Liability Partnerships Act (Cap. 163A);<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“officer of customs” has the meaning given by the Customs Act (Cap. 70);<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“owner” includes any person for the time being in charge of any wildlife (whether alive or dead), part of a wildlife, article, conveyance or other thing, and any person for the time being in occupation of any building;<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“place” means any public or private place and includes —<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">any land, whether built on or not;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">any body of water; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1DefNo">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pDefTxt">any area, whether or not enclosed, and whether above-ground, underground or underwater;<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“police officer” means a member of the Police Force or a special police officer, as defined in the Police Force Act (Cap. 235);<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“protected wildlife” means a wildlife that belongs to a protected wildlife species;<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“protected wildlife species” means a wildlife species prescribed as a protected wildlife species for the purposes of this Act;<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“reward” means any payment or other benefit (whether monetary or otherwise);<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“seized item” means any wildlife (whether dead or alive), part of a wildlife, article, conveyance or other thing seized by an enforcement officer under this Act;<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“wildlife” means an animal that belongs to a wildlife species, and includes the young or egg of the animal;<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="def" style="font-size:13pt">“wildlife species” means any species of animals of a wild nature, but excludes domestic dogs and cats, horses, cattle, sheep, goats, domestic pigs and poultry.<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></span></span></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr3-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Operation of other written laws</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>3.</strong><a name="pr3-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;To avoid doubt, nothing in this Act affects or limits the operation of the following written laws:<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the Animals and Birds Act (Cap. 7);</td></tr><tr><td 137);</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>l</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the Jurong Town Corporation Act (Cap. 150);</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>m</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the Parks and Trees Act (Cap. 216);</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>n</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the Public Utilities Act (Cap. 261);</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>o</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">the Sentosa Development Corporation Act (Cap. 291).</td></tr></tbody></table></span><a name="pr3-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;To also avoid doubt, nothing in this Act affects a police officer’s powers or duties under the Criminal Procedure Code (Cap. 68) or any other written law.<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr4-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Appointment of Director-General and authorised officers</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>4.</strong><a name="pr4-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Board is responsible for the administration of this Act, and to that end, the Board must appoint an officer of the Board to be the Director-General, Wildlife Management.</span><a name="pr4-ps2-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(2)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Director-General may, subject to the directions of the Board, appoint any of the following persons to be an authorised officer for the purpose of assisting the Director-General in administering and carrying out the provisions of this Act or any other written law which confers powers on the Director-General:<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">an employee of the Board;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">an employee of another statutory authority;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">a public officer;</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>d</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">an auxiliary police officer appointed under the Police Force Act (Cap.&nbsp;235).</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps3-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(3)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Director-General may delegate the exercise of all or any of the powers conferred or duties imposed upon the Director-General by any provision of this Act or any other written law (except the power of delegation conferred by this subsection) to an authorised officer; and any reference in the provision of this Act or any other written law to the Director-General includes a reference to such an authorised officer.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps4-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(4)&nbsp;&nbsp;Any delegation under subsection&nbsp;(3) may be general or in a particular case and may be subject to such conditions or limitations as set out in this Act or as the Board may specify.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps5-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(5)&nbsp;&nbsp;The Director-General may, for any reason that appears to him to be sufficient, at any time revoke a person’s appointment as an authorised officer.</td></tr></tbody></table><a name="pr4-ps6-"></a><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov2Txt">(6)&nbsp;&nbsp;A person mentioned in subsection&nbsp;(2)(<em>d</em>) who is appointed as an authorised officer does not, by virtue only of the appointment, become an employee or agent of the Board.<div class="amendNote">[Act 10 of 2019 wef 01/04/2019]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr4A-"><span class="noBold"></span><span class="">Authorised officers are public servants and public officers</span></td></tr></tbody></table><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Txt"><strong>4A.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Without affecting sections 20 and 21 of the Public Sector (Governance) Act 2018 (Act 5 of 2018), an authorised officer —<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">is taken to be a public servant for the purposes of the Penal Code (Cap. 224) when performing a function or exercising a power under this Act; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>b</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">is, in relation to the administration, assessment, collection or enforcement of payment of a composition sum under this Act, taken to be a public officer for the purposes of the Financial Procedure Act (Cap. 109); and section 20 of that Act applies to the authorised officer even though the authorised officer is not or was not in the employment of the Government.<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="prov1"><table width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="prov1Hdr" id="pr5-"><span class="noBold"></span><span condition the Director-General thinks fit; and</td></tr><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>c</em>)</td><td class="pTxt">in any form or manner the Director-General thinks fit (including by publishing the offence, to a fine not exceeding $10,000.<div class="amendNote">[Act 18 of 2020 wef 01/06/2020]</div></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div not exceeding 6 months or to both; and</td></tr><tr id="pr5C-ps3-p1b-p2ii-p3B-"><td class="p3No">(B)</td><td class="p3Txt">for a second or subsequent offence, to a fine not exceeding $20,000 or to class="prov1Txt"><strong>6.</strong><a name="pr6-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Nothing in this Act shall make it unlawful for the occupier or person in charge of any land to kill, class="prov1Txt"><strong>11B.</strong><a name="pr11B-ps1-"></a><span class="prov2TxtIL">—(1)&nbsp;&nbsp;Where an authorised officer or a police officer has reason to believe that an offence under this Act has been committed or is being committed, or where an officer of customs has reason to believe that an offence under this Act relating to import or export has been or is being committed, the authorised officer, police officer or officer of customs may seize the following:<table class="p1_1" style="font-size:13pt" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td class="p1No">(<em>a</em>)</td><td
